In re Yaccarino


D-28


Supreme Court of New Jersey


101 N.J. 342; 502 A.2d 3; 1985 N.J. LEXIS 2406


October 9, 1984, Argued  
December 27, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On an order to show cause why respondent should not be removed from judicial office.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Supreme Court of New Jersey issued an order to show cause why respondent judge should not be removed from judicial office after a special panel of the Advisory Committee on Judicial Conduct found that the evidence showed a pattern of misconduct that warranted removal from the bench.


OVERVIEW: Respondent judge was ordered to show cause why he should not be removed from office and thereafter the court ordered his removal from judicial office. The claims that the proceedings should have been dismissed in their entirety on constitutional and statutory grounds were without merit and were rejected. They did not violate due process rights as the investigatory, prosecutorial, and adjudicative functions were separated. The special panel was strictly ancillary and its recommendations were purely advisory. Although respondent had been a productive, conscientious, and energetic judge to whom significant and substantial judicial responsibilities had been assigned, his conduct threatened the whole concept of government under the law. It was repetitive, not episodic or aberrational. He allowed his personal and family interests to override judicial obligations and misused the judicial office for these reasons. Further, his conduct was wholly inconsistent with his judicial obligation to remain objective, impartial, and dignified. Finally, although he demonstrated that he suffered from a medical disability, it did not provide a defense to removal.


OUTCOME: The court ordered respondent judge removed from judicial office because his conduct, which consisted of serious professional and personal shortcomings, demonstrated his unfitness for continued judicial service and warranted his removal.

Abbott v. Burke


A-75


Supreme Court of New Jersey


100 N.J. 269; 495 A.2d 376; 1985 N.J. LEXIS 2372


November 27, 1984, Argued  
July 23, 1985, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Later proceeding at Abbott v. Burke, 117 N.J. 51, 563 A.2d 818, 1989 N.J. LEXIS 1090 (1989)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification to the Superior Court, Appellate Division, whose opinion is reported at 195 N.J. Super. 59 (1984).
Abbott v. Burke, 195 N.J. Super. 59, 477 A.2d 1278, 1984 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1033 (N.J. Super. Ct., 1984)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, board of education and state officials, sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court, Appellate Division (New Jersey), which remanded for trial a challenge to the Public School Education Act of 1975, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 18A:7A-1 to 18A:7A-33 filed by plaintiff school children.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff school children filed an action claiming that the Public School Education Act of 1975, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 18A:7A-1 to 18A:7A-33 was unconstitutional as funded. Defendants, board of education and state officials, moved to dismiss on the grounds that plaintiffs had failed to exhaust their administrative remedies. The court held that the presence of constitutional issues did not preclude resort to administrative adjudication because the complex factual issues presented would cause the litigation to turn on evidence that demanded close examination and evaluation. The court reversed and transferred the case to defendant commissioner of education because the issues of educational quality and municipal finance could be more effectively assessed by a tribunal with the particular training, acquired expertise, actual experience, and direct regulatory responsibility in those fields.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment remanding the matter for trial and transferred plaintiff school children's claims to defendant commissioner of education because constitutional claims did not preclude resort to administrative adjudication.

Barry v. Arrow Pontiac, Inc.


A-72


Supreme Court of New Jersey


100 N.J. 57; 494 A.2d 804; 1985 N.J. LEXIS 2354


January 22, 1985, Argued  
July 18, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court, Appellate Division, whose opinion is reported at 193 N.J. Super. 613 (1984).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant automobile dealer challenged the judgment of the Superior Court, Appellate Division (New Jersey), which affirmed the decision of respondent director of consumer affairs and held that appellant violated the Consumer Fraud Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 56:8-1 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Respondent director of consumer affairs contended that appellant automobile dealer's advertisement was misleading and deceptive to the consuming public in violation of the Consumer Fraud Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 56:8-1 et seq. The ad stated that many cars would be priced well below "dealer invoice." The court held that N.J. Admin. Code tit. 13:45A-2.2(a)(7)(iv) prohibited comparisons to the "dealer's cost" or "inventory price" in an advertisement. Appellant asserted that the term "dealer invoice" was not synonymous with either "dealer's cost" or "inventory price." However, the court reasoned that the term "dealer invoice" might be susceptible to the same misinterpretation by consumers because disagreement even existed among testifying experts at the administrative hearing. The issue was whether the ad itself was misleading to the average consumer, not whether it could later be explained to a more knowledgeable, inquisitive consumer. The court also found that N.J. Admin. Code tit. 13:45A-2.2(a)(7)(iv) was constitutionally valid in that it did not infringe on appellant's U.S. Const. amend. I rights to engage in commercial speech, and it was not vague or overbroad.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that adopted the decision of respondent director of consumer affairs. The court held that appellant automobile dealer's use of the term "dealer invoice" in its advertisement came within the scope and intendment of a Consumer Fraud Act regulation against commercial speech. The advertisement was misleading and deceptive to the consuming public.

Greenberg v. Kimmelman


A-86


Supreme Court of New Jersey


99 N.J. 552; 494 A.2d 294; 1985 N.J. LEXIS 2350


December 10, 1984, Argued  
July 2, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court, Appellate Division.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff spouse appealed from the decision of the Superior Court, Appellate Division (New Jersey), which affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of defendant State, sustaining the constitutionality of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 52:13D-17.2b, which prohibited state officers and employees, as well as their spouses, from employment with casinos.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff spouse was the wife of a superior court judge and was barred from casino employment. She challenged the constitutionality of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 52:13D-17.2b, an amendment to the New Jersey Conflicts of Interest Law, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 52:13D-12 to -27, which prohibited virtually all state officers and employees, including full-time members of the judiciary and their immediate families, from employment with casinos. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of defendant, the state, sustaining the constitutionality of the statute. The appellate court affirmed and plaintiff appealed. Upon review, the court concluded that the right to employment opportunity was a liberty interest protected against arbitrary governmental interference by the U.S. Const. amend. XIV, but that the right to a particular job was not fundamental. The statute was supported by a rational basis manifested by the state's interest in preserving the integrity of the judiciary and confidence in the casino industry. Finding the statute to be valid under the U.S. Constitution and the state constitution, the judgment of the appellate court was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court which affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of defendant, the state, sustaining the constitutionality of the prohibition against plaintiff spouse from employment with casinos because the state's interest in preserving the integrity of the judiciary and confidence in the casino industry was a rational basis to support the ban.

In re Bd. of Educ.


A-124


Supreme Court of New Jersey

Kramer v. Board of Education, 99 N.J. 173, 491 A.2d 681, 1984 N.J. LEXIS 3384 (1984)

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant teacher challenged the decision of the Public Employment Relations Commission (New Jersey), in her action against respondents, board of education, union representative, and teacher's union, for unfair labor practices. Appellant alleged that the amendments to the New Jersey Employer-Employee Relations Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 34:13A-5.1 to 21, requiring nonunion public employees to pay fees to the union were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant teacher filed a charge with the Public Employment Relations Commission alleging that respondent board of education had engaged in unfair practices by instituting an automatic payroll deduction for union representation fees without signed authorization cards, thereby interfering with her right to refrain from union activity, in violation of N.J. Ann. § 34:13A-5.6 was not unconstitutional on its face and prevented the constitutional violations alleged by appellant.

State v. Cameron


A-101-83


Supreme Court of New Jersey


100 N.J. 586; 498 A.2d 1217; 1985 N.J. LEXIS 2388


March 20, 1984, Argued  
June 19, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court, Appellate Division, whose opinion is reported at 189 N.J. Super. 404 (1983).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant minister appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court, Appellate Division (New Jersey) affirming the trial court's decision in favor of plaintiff government that defendant had violated a municipal zoning law, Franklin, N.J. Ordinance 832, § 504.1 (1976), by temporarily using his home to hold weekly religious services. Defendant claimed that the ordinance did not clearly forbid this religious activity and was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Defendant minister used his home to hold religious services for his congregation until a permanent location could be found. The zoning law where defendant lived, Franklin, N.J. Ordinance 832, § 404 (1976), designated different zone classifications for land use in the town. Section 504.1 of the ordinance provided that the only permitted use in the area of defendant's home was single-family houses, and churches and similar places of worship were excluded. The township charged defendant with violating § 504.1 and the trial court, following a trial de novo, also held that defendant violated the ordinance by using his home as a church. Defendant appealed, contending that the ordinance was impermissibly vague under the Federal Constitution, U.S. Const. amend. V, and the State Constitution, N.J. Const. art. I, par. 1. The lower court affirmed on appeal and defendant sought further review. The court found that the phrase "churches and similar places of worship" rendered the ordinance vague as applied against defendant because its indefinite meaning failed to provide adequate warning or specific guidelines for fair enforcement. The decision was reversed and defendant's conviction set aside.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and ordered that defendant's conviction for violating a local ordinance be set aside. The court found that the ordinance, as applied to defendant in the circumstances, was vague and unenforceable as a matter of constitutional due process.

South Hamilton Associates v. Morristown


A-77


Supreme Court of New Jersey


99 N.J. 437; 493 A.2d 523; 1985 N.J. LEXIS 2335


March 5, 1985, Argued  
June 17, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court, Appellate Division.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant municipality appealed a judgment of the Superior Court, Appellate Division (New Jersey) that reversed the trial court's order that dismissed plaintiff landlord's complaint seeking a declaration that retroactive provisions of rent control ordinance were null and void.


OVERVIEW: Defendant municipality passed a vacancy decontrol ordinance and later attempted to repeal it by enacting a second ordinance. The second ordinance was defective because a majority of council members did not vote, so the council retroactively enacted a third ordinance, Morristown, N.J., Ordinance No. 0-25-82, to correct the defective ordinance. During the period between the second and third ordinances, plaintiff landlord leased units to new tenants at higher rents permitted under the first ordinance. Defendant claimed that plaintiff had to roll back these rents under the retroactive provisions of the third ordinance. Plaintiff objected and sought a declaration that the third ordinance's retroactive provisions were null and void. The trial court dismissed the complaint but the lower court reversed and held that the retroactive provisions were invalid. Defendant sought further review and the court affirmed, finding that retroactive application of the third ordinance was not supported by a rational public purpose and unconstitutionally impaired plaintiff's contract rights. The court upheld the leases entered into by plaintiff during the period in which vacancy decontrol was in effect.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, holding that the retroactive application of the rent control ordinance was invalid. The court found that the circumstances did not constitute a rational public purpose sufficient to permit defendant municipality to apply the ordinance retroactively and impair plaintiff landlord's contract rights.

Keyes Martin & Co. v. Director, Div. of Purchase & Property, Dep't of Treasury


A-91


Supreme Court of New Jersey


99 N.J. 244; 491 A.2d 1236; 1985 N.J. LEXIS 2327


December 10, 1984, Argued  
May 6, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from and certification to the Superior Court, Appellate Division, whose opinion is reported at 196 N.J. Super. 52 (1984).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, state and director of purchase and property division, challenged a decision of the Superior Court (New Jersey), which vacated appellant director's decision awarding a contract to provide advertising for the state lottery to a party other than respondent company.


OVERVIEW: In an effort to obtain a contract with the state lottery commission, respondent company submitted the lowest bid to appellants, state and director of purchase and property division. Respondent's bid was rejected because the lottery commission was informed of suspect business dealings between respondent and the chairman of the lottery commission. Appellant reversed and awarded respondent the contract. On appeal, the court reversed and reinstated appellant's decision rejecting respondent's bid. The court held that appellant was given broad discretionary power under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 52:34-12(d) and could refuse to award a contract for advertising services to respondent when such action was in the public interest, and was based on the appearance of wrongdoing attributable to a possible conflict of interest involving the bidder and a member of the contracting agency.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court, which awarded a state advertising contract to respondent company, and held that appellants, state and director of purchase and property division, had discretion to reject respondent's bid.

In re In re Burlington County Bd. of Chosen Freeholders


A-68


Supreme Court of New Jersey


99 N.J. 90; 491 A.2d 631; 1985 N.J. LEXIS 2328


December 13, 1983, Argued  
May 6, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification to the Superior Court, Appellate Division, whose opinion is reported at 190 N.J. Super. 256 (1983).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant county sheriff challenged a decision of the Superior Court (New Jersey), which affirmed the decision of the trial court that held that plaintiff county board of chosen freeholder's allegations of irregularities in the operation of defendant's office could be impartially investigated under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40A:5-22. Defendant contended that § 40A:5-22 was inapplicable and that to permit an investigation was an abuse of discretion.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff county board of chosen freeholder filed a resolution with the trial court requesting a summary investigation into defendant county sheriff's office under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40A:5-22, alleging serious misconduct of defendant's office. Defendant filed a counter-affidavit, contending § 40A:5-22 was not applicable to his office under the state constitution and that an order permitting investigation would be an abuse of discretion. The trial court ruled in favor of plaintiff, stating that they had sufficiently established their belief that serious misconduct had occurred in connection with the operation of defendant's office. The superior court affirmed the trial court's decision. On certification, the court affirmed the lower courts' decisions, finding that § 40A:5-22 permitted a judge, in his discretion and response to a petition of 25 taxpayers or a resolution of the governing body, to make a summary investigation into the affairs of any local unit. The court stated that the state constitution did not protect defendant from investigation and that plaintiff had established a prima facie case against defendant and, therefore, the investigation was properly ordered.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, finding that the state constitution did not protect defendant county sheriff from investigation and that plaintiff county board of chosen freeholder's had sufficiently established their belief that serious misconduct had occurred with the operation of defendant's office. The court stated that plaintiff had established a prima facie case against defendant and, therefore, the trial court properly ordered a summary investigation.

Rutherford Education Asso. v. Board of Education


(A-45) (A-67)


Supreme Court of New Jersey


99 N.J. 8; 489 A.2d 1148; 1985 N.J. LEXIS 2237


November 26, 1984, Argued  
April 11, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification to the Superior Court, Appellate Division.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated appeal, plaintiff teachers sought certified review of various decisions from the Superior Court, Appellate Division (New Jersey), denying plaintiffs various benefits retroactively payable to tenured Title I teachers by defendant local school boards under the state's judicial Spiewak rule.


OVERVIEW: In cases consolidated for certified review, plaintiff teachers challenged the appellate division's refusal to retroactively apply a prior decision of the state's highest court in favor of plaintiffs by awarding tenure benefits. Plaintiffs were Title 1 tenured teachers who had filed administrative petitions with the state's Commissioner of Education against defendant local school boards seeking various tenure benefits prior to the date that the Spiewak rule was announced by the state's highest court. Upon review, the state's highest court held that, in general, the Spiewak rule was prospectively applicable. However, because plaintiffs had pending petitions at the time the Spiewak rule was decided, the rule was retroactively applicable to require defendants to calculate tenure benefits for six years prior to the date that the ruling in the instant case was made. Only those plaintiffs who had been terminated before the date the Spiewak rule was announced were exempt from this limited retroactive application of the rule. The court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded for determination of successful plaintiffs' emoluments of tenure.


OUTCOME: The state's highest court affirmed the appellate court's decision refusing to order payment of benefits to plaintiff teachers who had been terminated by defendant local school boards before the date the Spiewak rule was announced. The court reversed as to all other plaintiffs and retroactively ordered payment of tenure benefits that had accrued in the six years prior to announcement of the instant decision.

American Bank & Trust Co. v. Lott


A-53


Supreme Court of New Jersey


99 N.J. 32; 490 A.2d 308; 1985 N.J. LEXIS 2236


November 5, 1984, Argued  
April 10, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court, Appellate Division, whose opinion is reported at 193 N.J. Super. 516 (1984).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant property owners challenged the denial of their motion to dismiss from the Superior Court, Appellate Division (New Jersey), in a mortgage foreclosure action brought by plaintiff foreign bank. Defendants argued that plaintiff failed to comply with the Corporation Business Activities Reporting Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 14A:13.


OVERVIEW: The issue was whether plaintiff foreign bank, notwithstanding its failure to comply with the filing requirements of the Corporation Business Activities Reporting Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 14A:13-14, could maintain a mortgage foreclosure action. Plaintiff sued to foreclose mortgages on property owned by defendant property owners. Defendants moved to dismiss the complaint because plaintiff had neither filed a notice of business activities report as required by N.J. Stat. Ann. § 14A:13-15, nor qualified for an exemption from filing by obtaining a certificate of authority to do business as permitted by N.J. Stat. Ann. § 14A:13-16a. The trial court denied defendants' motion. The Appellate Division concluded that a certificate of authority to act as an executor, testamentary trustee, or guardian, issued by the New Jersey Commissioner of Banking to plaintiff, satisfied the Reporting Act exemption. The judgment was affirmed because the court held that the legislature did not intend the Reporting Act to apply to foreign banks. Further, where the Reporting Act did not apply, its requirements were irrelevant to the determination whether plaintiff could maintain the present action.


OUTCOME: The denial of defendant property owners' motion to dismiss the complaint brought by plaintiff foreign bank for mortgage foreclosure was affirmed because plaintiff's compliance with the Corporation Business Activities Reporting Act was irrelevant to the lawsuit with defendants. The court noted that the Act did not apply to plaintiff.

 

250 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. 1979 Pontiac Trans Am


A-35


Supreme Court of New Jersey


98 N.J. 474; 487 A.2d 722; 1985 N.J. LEXIS 2228


October 23, 1984, Argued  
February 21, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification to the Superior Court, Appellate Division.
State v. 1979 Pontiac Trans Am,, 96 N.J. 299, 475 A.2d 592, 1984 N.J. LEXIS 2584 (1984)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant car owner sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court, Appellate Division (New Jersey), which, without taking testimony, forfeited appellant's car under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:64-1 et seq., for its use by his son in the commission of a theft. Appellant argued that he had no knowledge that the car was to be used in criminal activity.


OVERVIEW: Appellant car owner's son borrowed his father's car for the evening and committed a theft. Respondent state brought an in rem action to forfeit the auto, and, without hearing testimony, the trial court ordered vesting of the title in the county. Appellant sought review and argued that he had no knowledge that the car was to be used by his son in criminal activity. The court reversed, remanded for a plenary hearing, and ruled that, while N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:64-5 exempted only the property of innocent lessors and lienholders from forfeiture, the exemption was to be liberally construed to include other innocent owners who proved that they were uninvolved in and unaware of the wrongful activity, and that they had done all that reasonably could be expected to prevent the proscribed use of their property. The court held that with such liberal construction, the statute survived a constitutional attack that it constituted an unlawful taking of property without just compensation. The court remanded for the trial court to consider all of the relevant circumstances as related to appellant's knowledge of the illicit use of the car and his exercise of due care to prevent that use.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the trial court's judgment forfeiting appellant car owner's car. The court held that an exemption from forfeiture of property of innocent lessors and lienholders was construed to include any other innocent owners without prior notice or reason to know of the property's criminal use, thus saving the forfeiture statute from effecting an unconstitutional taking without compensation.

Horsemen's Benevolent & Protective Asso., New Jersey Div. v. Atlantic City Racing Asso.


A-12/13


Supreme Court of New Jersey


98 N.J. 445; 487 A.2d 707; 1985 N.J. LEXIS 2227


October 10, 1984, Argued  
February 14, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from and certification to the Superior Court, Appellate Division.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff horsemen's association appealed a decision of the Superior Court, Appellate Division (New Jersey), which held that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 5:5-66 was constitutional, but reversed plaintiff's judgment for statutory payments. In cross-appeals, plaintiff argued that defendant racetrack was estopped from contesting payment and was required to repay horse owners for deductions from winnings. Defendant argued that the statute was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff horsemen's association brought suit against defendant racetrack for underpayments to plaintiff under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 5:5-66 and the trial court entered judgment for plaintiff. The lower court reversed but ruled that defendant was required to repay owners for purse deductions. In cross-appeals, plaintiff argued that defendant was estopped from paying plaintiff less than the maximum allowed by § 5:5-66, and that defendant was required to repay horse owners for purse deductions made to pay plaintiff. Defendant argued that § 5:5-66 was unconstitutional. The court modified and affirmed, ruling that the statute was constitutional and a reasonable exercise of the police power because payments authorized by § 5:5-66 served the public purpose of aiding New Jersey horsemen and were not paid from the state treasury but were simply diverted from bets made by racetrack customers. The court also held that defendant's past practice of paying the maximum allowed contribution to plaintiff did not act to estop defendant from later paying less, and that defendant was not required to repay purse deductions made for the benefit of plaintiff.


OUTCOME: The court modified and affirmed the lower court's judgment. The court ruled that the statutory requirement of payments to plaintiff horsemen's association served a public purpose, did not use public funds, and was constitutional. The court held that defendant racetrack was not estopped from reducing its payments to plaintiff and that defendant was not required to repay purse deductions made to benefit plaintiff.

The court held that the case had to be litigated at the trial level.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case to the trial court without undertaking further review on the merits as to defendant development commission's moratorium on development of land, which included that of plaintiff landowners. The court held that the facts relied upon by the appellate court had substantially changed, requiring the case to be litigated at the trial level.

Phillips v. State, Dep't of Defense


A-24/25


Supreme Court of New Jersey


98 N.J. 235; 486 A.2d 318; 1985 N.J. LEXIS 2220


September 24, 1984, Argued  
January 21, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification to the Superior Court, Appellate Division.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant injured soldier and cross-appellant vehicle manufacturer sought review of a decision by the Superior Court (New Jersey), which held that an action in negligence could not lie against appellee soldiers and that appellant injured soldier's exclusive remedy against appellee state department of defense was under the military compensation law, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 38A:13-1.


OVERVIEW: Appellant injured soldier was hurt in a vehicle accident while on duty with the state militia under the command of appellee state department of defense. Appellant filed suit against appellee soldiers in negligence and against cross-appellant vehicle manufacturer. The trial court entered a summary judgment that appellant's exclusive remedy against appellee state department was under the military compensation law, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 38A:13-1, and found that appellee soldiers were not liable in negligence because they were acting within the scope of their duty when the accident occurred. Cross-appellant sought to receive indemnification from appellee soldiers. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court rejected the proposition that provisions of the Workers Compensation Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 34:15-7, were incorporated into the military compensation law such that appellee soldiers could be held liable in negligence if they were not complying with a lawful order. The court held that cross-appellant's action against the state had to fail because there was no statutory provision that permitted them to receive any indemnification.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court found that appellee state department of defense should have processed appellant injured soldier's claim. The court held that appellant and cross-appellant vehicle manufacturer was entitled to maintain their claims against appellee soldiers based on negligence for causing the accident.

Newark Superior Officers Asso. v. Newark


A-14


Supreme Court of New Jersey


98 N.J. 212; 486 A.2d 305; 1985 N.J. LEXIS 2215


October 10, 1984, Argued  
January 14, 1985, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court, Appellate Division, whose opinion is reported at 187 N.J. Super. 390 (1982).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, city, municipal council, and public officials, challenged a decision of the Superior Court, Appellate Division (New Jersey), which affirmed the trial court judgment that N.J. Stat. Ann. §40:69A-60.7 was unconstitutional special legislation, creating classifications based on population.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, an organization of deputy police chiefs, filed suit against defendants, city, municipal council, and public officials, alleging that legislation allowing the mayors of certain cities to appoint their police chiefs was unconstitutional, because it created a classification based on population. The appellate division affirmed the trial court's holding that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40:69A-60.7 was unconstitutional because it was special legislation. On review, the court reversed, holding that § 40:69A-60.7 had a rational basis for limiting the scope of the statute to the police chiefs of municipalities with the largest populations, because the volume of law enforcement problems facing the police director in larger cities created circumstances that did not exist in smaller cities. The court severed the grandfather clause as special legislation with no rational basis.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of plaintiffs, an organization of deputy police chiefs, and held in favor of defendants, city, municipal council, and public officials, finding that there was a rational basis for creating a classification based on population.

Mahwah v. Bergen County Bd. of Taxation


A-9/10/11


Supreme Court of New Jersey


98 N.J. 268; 486 A.2d 818; 1985 N.J. LEXIS 2216


October 10, 1984, Argued  
January 14, 1985, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Demarest v. Mahwah, 471 U.S. 1136, 105 S. Ct. 2677, 86 L. Ed. 2d 696, 1985 U.S. LEXIS 2098 (1985)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from and certification to the Superior Court, Appellate Division, whose opinion is reported at 190 N.J. Super. 84 (1983).
Mahwah v. Bergen County Bd. of Taxation, 190 N.J. Super. 84, 461 A.2d 1210, 1983 N.J. Super. LEXIS 867 (N.J. Super. Ct., 1983)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant township challenged a decision of the Superior Court (New Jersey), which affirmed the tax court's ruling that both rebate statutes, N.J. Stat. Ann. §54:4-5 and its supplemental statute, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:4-5.2, were unconstitutional special legislation and dismissed appellant's claims of rebate of half of its county taxes. Appellant argued that the above statutes qualified it for rebate for tax years 1978-1980.


OVERVIEW: Appellant township filed a petition with appellee county board of taxation requesting a rebate of half its county taxes pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:4-5 and for the year 1980 appellant sought payment of rebate or a declaration of tax-exempt status. Appellee denied relief and on appeal, the tax court held that both § 54:4-5 and its supplemental statute, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:4-5.2, were unconstitutional as special legislation and that appellant had failed to established the necessary acreage for the tax years 1978-1980 to qualify under § 54:4-5. The superior court affirmed the tax court's decision. On appeal, the court reversed the superior court's judgment, finding that the tax court erred in its determination that state-owned property could not be considered in its calculation for a county tax rebate and stated that the rebate statute had been amended by the legislature twice and that legislature's intention was that the two statutes should co-exist. The court, thus, held that appellant had the necessary acreage to qualify under § 54:4-5. The court affirmed the superior court's finding that the supplemental statute could be severed from the rebate statute, which remained valid.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the superior court's decision, finding that the tax court erred in its determination that state-owned property could not be considered in its calculation for a county tax rebate and that the statute did not contain an express repealer of the rebate statute, which had been amended by the legislature constantly. The court affirmed the superior court's finding that the supplemental statute could be severed from the rebate statute.

State v. White


A-26


Supreme Court of New Jersey


98 N.J. 122; 484 A.2d 691; 1984 N.J. LEXIS 3259


October 9, 1984, Argued  
December 20, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification to the Superior Court, Appellate Division.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his sentence, that was enhanced under the Graves Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:43-6c, following his convictions of armed robbery, conspiracy, and weapons possession charges and affirmed by the Superior Court, Appellate Division (New Jersey). Appellant asserted that the application of the enhancements to an accomplice who did not actually use the weapon during the offense was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed appellant's sentence after his convictions of armed robbery, conspiracy to commit armed robbery, possession of a weapon for an unlawful purpose, and possession of a defaced weapon. Appellant was convicted as an accomplice to two separate robberies where one of his co-defendants used a gun during the commission of the offenses. The court held that when an accomplice was found guilty of an offense that was committed with a firearm, he was subject to sentencing enhancements under the Graves Act (the Act), N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:43-6c. The court held further that if an accomplice was convicted only of an unarmed offense, but the trial court found that the defendant nonetheless knew or had reason to know that his cohort would use or be in possession of a firearm in the commission of the offense, the accomplice was again subject to the Act's penalties. The court rejected appellant's argument that the Act was unconstitutional for failure to give fair notice. The court found that application the Act to accomplices was constitutional and served the general purposes of sentencing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's sentence as enhanced. The court held that an accomplice convicted of the armed offense or one convicted of the unarmed offense who knew that his co-defendant would use a firearm were subject to the provisions of the statute. The court held that the application of the statute to accomplices was not unconstitutional when it served the general purposes of sentencing.

Fairlawn Shopper v. Director, Division of Taxation


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New Jersey


98 N.J. 64; 484 A.2d 659; 1984 N.J. LEXIS 3266; 10 Media L. Rep. 2489


November 28, 1983, Argued  
October 4, 1984, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated tax appeals, the court addressed the applicability of the New Jersey Sales and Use Tax Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:32B-1 to -29 (Act), to the amounts expended by the appellant printers for certain outside printing costs in their publication of free-circulation newspapers. Appellants contended they were entitled to an exemption because their sales receipts and sales for resale were exempted from the Act.


OVERVIEW: Appellant printers filed suit against respondent taxation division. The tax court found that the exemption afforded by N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:32B-8(e) was not intended to exempt newspapers as they passed between printer and publisher. The appeals court reversed the tax court judgment. Appellant sought and was granted certification to determine the impact of the New Jersey Sales and Use Tax Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:32B-1 to -29 (Act), on the free-circulation newspaper industry. The appeal posed two issues concerning tax exemptions. The court had to determine what constituted a newspaper for purposes of the Act and reviewed the "sale for resale" exemption of the Act to discern its effect on free-circulation publication. The court concluded that the Act required some consideration to pass during the transfer of title or possession, although the Act was unclear as to the source of the consideration. The court reversed the appeals court judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appeals court judgment against appellant printers and for respondent taxation division. The court found that the definition of "sale" in the New Jersey Sales and Use Tax Act meant that the consideration required to satisfy the definition of a sale had to be based upon third parties. The court agreed with the trial court that appellant's purchases were exempt.

Karcher v. Kean


A-119/144/145


Supreme Court of New Jersey


97 N.J. 483; 479 A.2d 403; 1984 N.J. LEXIS 2701


March 20, 1984, Argued  
August 6, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court, Appellate Division, whose opinion is reported at 190 N.J. Super. 197 (1983).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants and appellee governor challenged an order of the Superior Court of New Jersey ruling that the appellee had properly exercised the line-item veto power with respect to several controverted provisions in an appropriations act, but that the appellee had also exceeded his power in vetoing certain other provisions.


OVERVIEW: Appellee governor exercised the line-item veto to several provisions of an appropriations act. Appellants brought suit, contending that the appellee exceeded the constitutional authority vested in him. The intermediate court ruled that while most of the vetoes comported with the law, the appellee had exceeded his authority in some instances. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part, finding that all of the line-item vetoes were properly exercised. Pursuant to N.J. Const. art. V, § I, para. 15, the appellee was constitutionally empowered to object to any item or items included in an appropriation bill through the exercise of a selective veto. The appellee appropriately exercised this power with respect to provisions relating to state aid to municipalities. He also properly exercised the right in striking certain highway appropriations and the vetoes did not constitute unlawful affirmative use of the power. Additionally, general conditions on appropriated funds were part of an appropriation and also within the ambit of the appellee's veto power.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed in part and reversed in part. All of appellee governor's line-item vetoes of the appropriations act comported with the law and none exceeded the constitutional authority vested in him.

Metromedia, Inc. v. Director, Division of Taxation


A-9


Supreme Court of New Jersey


97 N.J. 313; 478 A.2d 742; 1984 N.J. LEXIS 2694


November 7, 1983, Argued  
July 23, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On Certification to the Superior Court, Appellate Division, whose opinion is reported at 187 N.J. Super. 562 (1983).



DISPOSITION:  The judgment of the appellate court reversing the tax court's determination in favor of appellant taxpayer was reversed and the judgment of the tax court was reinstated. Although appellee division of taxation director was given statutory authority to modify the method of tax base computation, the method he used required prior rule promulgation under the Administrative Procedure Act.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer challenged the judgment of the Superior Court, Appellate Division (New Jersey) reversing the tax court's ruling in appellant's favor following appellant's challenge to the tax deficiency assessment made by appellee division of taxation director.


OVERVIEW: Under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:10A-8, appellee division of taxation director modified the method for determining appellant taxpayer's tax base based on an audience share allocation method. The tax court held that the method used constituted a rule within the meaning of the Administrative Procedure Act (APA), N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 52:14B-1 to 15, necessitating compliance with the statutory requirements of the APA governing the adoption of agency rules. The appellate court reversed, holding that appellee's actions were authorized by § 54:10A-8. On review, the court reversed and reinstated the tax court ruling. The court recognized that the language of § 54:10A-8 granted appellee needed broad authority to modify the statutory formula for determining a multi-state taxpayer's New Jersey tax base by which the tax was measured. But, the court held that the action taken by appellee was invalid absent the prior promulgation of rules in compliance with the APA, and that the actual determination to use such an allocation method required implementing regulations and recourse to rule-making procedures.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court reversing the tax court's determination in favor of appellant taxpayer was reversed and the judgment of the tax court was reinstated. Although appellee division of taxation director was given statutory authority to modify the method of tax base computation, the method he used required prior rule promulgation under the Administrative Procedure Act.

Airwork Serv. Div., Div. of Pac. Airmotive Corp. v. Director, Division of Taxation

November 7, 1983, Argued  
July 23, 1984, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Airwork Service Div. v. Director, Div. of Taxation, 471 U.S. 1127, 105 S. Ct. 2662, 86 L. Ed. 2d 278, 1985 U.S. LEXIS 2048 (1985)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification to the Superior Court, Appellate Division.
Airwork Service Div. v. Director, Div. of Taxation, 4 N.J. Tax 532, 1982 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1055 (App.Div., 1982)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court (New Jersey) that affirmed the trial court's grant of partial summary judgment in favor of respondent, the director of the New Jersey Department of Taxation. The court held that airplane repair services rendered by appellant for out-of-state customers were subject to state sales tax.


OVERVIEW: Appellant corporation repaired airplane engines and often returned them to out-of-state customers. Respondent, the director of the New Jersey Division of Taxation, sought to assess sales tax on the services. When appellant sought review, the tax court granted partial summary judgment in favor of respondent, holding that the assessment was valid. The lower appellate court affirmed. Appellant sought further review and asserted that because many provisions of the New Jersey Sales and Use Tax Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:32B-1 to -29, treated the sale of goods and services equivalently and only sales of goods within the state were taxed, the legislature could not have intended to tax services performed on goods to be delivered to out-of-state customers. Appellant also contended that because respondent had not attempted to collect the taxes in previous years, respondent was estopped from beginning to collect the tax. The court noted that the application of the principles of estoppel was generally inappropriate where the collection of taxes by a public body was involved. The court held the tax was valid and affirmed the judgment of the lower court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the court below because it held that the assessment of a state sales tax on services rendered in New Jersey on airplane engines owned by out-of-state customers was valid.

Trus Joist Corp. v. Treetop Assocs.


A-135/136


Supreme Court of New Jersey


97 N.J. 22; 477 A.2d 817; 1984 N.J. LEXIS 2685


March 20, 1984, Argued  
July 12, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification to Superior Court, Appellate Division.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bank sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court, Appellate Division (New Jersey), which held appellant's mortgage on a fraudulently conveyed property invalid in favor of respondent bankruptcy trustee.


OVERVIEW: Appellant bank loaned money to the grantee of property that was held to be fraudulently conveyed. The loan was secured by a mortgage on the property against which a lis pendens had been filed several months earlier, giving notice of an action to have the conveyance declared void and a judgment declared as a lien on the property. Respondent bankruptcy trustee filed a motion to set aside appellant's mortgage. The lower court held appellant's mortgage partially invalid, stating that the rights of respondent as a creditor related back to the filing of the earlier lis pendens. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that the effect of a notice of lis pendens in this context was limited to preservation of the rights of the party filing it. The court said that the test of when new matters could be related back to an earlier notice of lis pendens was whether the parties, the property to be affected, and the general purpose and subject of the lawsuit were the same. The court stated that the first and third factors were different; therefore, the new matters asserted by respondent did not relate back, and appellant's mortgage could not be invalidated.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the lower court and held that respondent bankruptcy trustee's action to set aside appellant bank's mortgage could not be related back to the prior filing of a notice of lis pendens by one creditor. Therefore the mortgage could not be held invalid.

263 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rockholt


A-24


Supreme Court of New Jersey


96 N.J. 570; 476 A.2d 1236; 1984 N.J. LEXIS 2712; 52 A.L.R.4th 757


January 24, 1984, Argued  
June 27, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification to the Superior Court, Appellate Division, whose opinion is reported at 186 N.J. Super. 539 (1982).
State v. Rockholt, 186 N.J. Super. 539, 453 A.2d 258, 1982 N.J. Super. LEXIS 939 (App.Div., 1982)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment from the Superior Court (New Jersey) that upheld his convictions of misconduct in office for selling a motorcycle owned by the police department, receiving stolen police identification cards, and distributing a controlled dangerous substance. Appellant contended that the entrapment defense under the New Jersey Code of Criminal Justice, N.J. Stat. Ann. 2C:2-12, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted appellant of misconduct in office for selling a motorcycle owned by the police department, receiving stolen police identification cards, and distributing a controlled dangerous substance. The court affirmed the superior court judgment that sustained appellant's convictions. The court disagreed with appellant's contention that, because the entrapment defense of the New Jersey Code of Criminal Justice, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:2-12, placed the burden of proving entrapment upon him, it violated the requirement that the state prove every element of an offense beyond a reasonable doubt. The court ruled that although the state must establish an offense, it was not constitutionally required to show the absence of entrapment beyond a reasonable doubt. The court found that the jury charge properly described the burden of proof for the entrapment defense. The court found that any confusion caused by the jury charge was beneficial to appellant. The court found that the jury charge on objective entrapment helped appellant. The court found that the jury charge clearly provided that whether appellant was predisposed to perpetrate the offense was a jury question.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court judgment that upheld appellant's convictions of misconduct in office for selling a motorcycle owned by the police department, receiving stolen police identification cards, and distributing a controlled dangerous substance. The entrapment defense was found constitutional because the state only had the burden of proving the offenses beyond a reasonable doubt and did not have to show the absence of entrapment.

 

264 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Coons v. American Honda Motor Co.


A-87


Supreme Court of New Jersey


96 N.J. 419; 476 A.2d 763; 1984 N.J. LEXIS 2689


January 24, 1984, Argued  
June 13, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On a rehearing of a portion of the judgment of this Court, dated August 3, 1983 and reported at 94 N.J. 307 (1983). See 95 N.J. 234 (1984).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On petition for rehearing of a prior appeal, plaintiff injured party, supported by amici curiae, alleged that the court erred in giving retrospective effect to a decision in, which declared the tolling provision of the statute of limitations in actions against defendant foreign corporation, N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 2A:14-22, unconstitutional in an action for personal injuries.


OVERVIEW: In an action for personal injury, the court gave retroactive effect to its decision in a prior appeal that found the tolling provision of the statute of limitations in actions against a foreign corporation, N.J. Stat. Ann. §§ 2A:14-22 unconstitutional. Plaintiff injured party, supported by amici curiae, sought rehearing. The court directed defendant foreign corporation, supported by amici curiae, to respond only on the issue of retroactivity. Applying an equitable balancing test, the court reversed, in part, and held, as a matter of law, that the earlier decision invalidating a civil statute was to be applied prospectively from the date of the decision. It concluded that the ruling established a new principle of law. At the time plaintiff started his action, the tolling provision for foreign unrepresented corporations was in effect; after the decision there was no such provision. The reliance of plaintiff and those similarly situated that under the statute their actions would be preserved, and the absence of a demonstrated burden to defendant and corporate amici, supported a prospective application of the decision.


OUTCOME: The court modified its prior judgment, applied retrospectively, that invalidated the tolling provision of a civil statute of limitations as to foreign unrepresented corporations and made it effective as of the date of the decision. Establishing a new rule of law and balancing the reliance of plaintiff injured party and the lack of burden on defendant foreign corporation supported a prospective application of the decision.

Canino v. New York News, Inc.


A-90/91


Supreme Court of New Jersey


96 N.J. 189; 475 A.2d 528; 1984 N.J. LEXIS 2677; 42 A.L.R.4th 263; 10 Media L. Rep. 1852


February 6, 1984, Argued  
May 29, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court, Appellate Division.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, newspaper and reporter, challenged a judgment of the Superior Court (New Jersey) that sustained the denial by the trial court of appellants' motion to dismiss, which allowed the libel action of appellees, decedent and executrix, to continue after appellee decedent had deceased.


OVERVIEW: Appellees, decedent and executrix, brought a libel action against appellants, newspaper and reporter, because of appellants' published article that linked decedent to organized crime, to which appellants responded with a motion to dismiss after appellee decedent passed away. The court affirmed the judgment of the superior court that upheld the denial of appellants' motion for dismissal by the trial court. The court ruled that the clause "trespass to the person" found in the Survival Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:15-3, included tort actions for libel and slander. The court determined that the issue of whether appellees' action should properly survive after appellee decedent's passing did not involve considerations of the U.S. Const. amend. I, which were already included within the prescribed scope of defamation law. The court held that appellees' action survived the decease of the injured party, appellee decedent, because the common law considered this libel to qualify as a trespass on the person under § 2A:15-3. The court concluded that this principle was consistent with its values and did not violate any of appellants' constitutional freedoms under the U.S. Const. amend. I.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the superior court that affirmed the denial of the motion to dismiss brought by appellants, newspaper and reporter, against the libel action of appellees, decedent and executrix. The lower courts properly allowed this action to proceed beyond the decease of appellee decedent because this libel constituted a common law trespass and appellants' constitutional freedoms were not abrogated.

State v. Lee


A-69


Supreme Court of New Jersey


96 N.J. 156; 475 A.2d 31; 1984 N.J. LEXIS 2420


November 29, 1983, Argued  
May 7, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification to the Superior Court, Appellate Division, whose opinion is reported at 188 N.J. Super. 432 (1982).
State v. Wright, 96 N.J. 170, 475 A.2d 38, 1984 N.J. LEXIS 2424 (1984)
State v. Lee, 188 N.J. Super. 432, 457 A.2d 1184, 1982 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1023 (App.Div., 1982)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the opinion of the Superior Court, Appellate Division (New Jersey), which sustained defendant's conviction for the offense of possession of a weapon under circumstances not manifestly appropriate for such lawful use as it may have, pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:39-5d.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of possession of a weapon under circumstances not manifestly appropriate for such lawful use as it may have, pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:39-5d, after he was found to be in possession of scissors taped together to form a stiletto. The appellate division affirmed. The court affirmed, finding that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:39-5d did not require intent to harm and was not overbroad or vague. The court found that possession of a weapon with intent to harm was instead prohibited by N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:39-4d, and surrounding circumstances reflected that the object was not manifestly appropriate for lawful use. The court concluded that the statute was not overbroad as it did not impinge upon any U.S. Const. amend. I rights, and affected only the knowing possession of a weapon under circumstances not manifestly appropriate for lawful uses. The court found that the statute was not vague, as the words were a sufficient warning so that an ordinary person was apprised with a reasonable degree of certainty of that which was proscribed, and law enforcement officers were on notice that mere possession of a potential weapon was not sufficient to justify an arrest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate division's judgment affirming defendant's conviction for possession of a weapon under circumstances not manifestly appropriate for such lawful use as it may have, because the statute did not require intent and was not overbroad or vague.

State v. Wright


A-18/19


Supreme Court of New Jersey


96 N.J. 170; 475 A.2d 38; 1984 N.J. LEXIS 2424


November 29, 1983, Argued  
May 7, 1984, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Companion case at State v. Lee, 96 N.J. 156, 475 A.2d 31, 1984 N.J. LEXIS 2420 (1984)
Appeal dismissed by Wright v. New Jersey, 469 U.S. 1146, 105 S. Ct. 890, 83 L. Ed. 2d 906, 1985 U.S. LEXIS 502 (1985)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification to the Superior Court, Appellate Division.
State v. Wright, 187 N.J. Super. 160, 453 A.2d 1352, 1982 N.J. Super. LEXIS 968 (App.Div., 1982)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court, Appellate Division (New Jersey), which reversed defendant's conviction under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:39-5d for possessing a weapon under circumstances not manifestly appropriate for lawful uses.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was observed on a street corner by police officers who knew that he was the subject of several outstanding arrest warrants. Defendant was arrested and a search was conducted. The search revealed an Exacto knife strapped to defendant's ankle. Defendant was convicted of knowingly possessing a weapon under circumstances not manifestly appropriate for such lawful uses as it may have, pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:39-5d. The conviction was reversed by the appellate court on the ground that the charge given the jury was inadequate, and the statute was unconstitutionally overbroad or vague. The court held that proof of intent to use a weapon for unlawful purposes was not necessary to save the statute from a challenge of unconstitutionality. Therefore, the court reversed the judgment of the appellate court and reinstated defendant's conviction because the charge delivered by the trial court was adequate.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was reversed and defendant's conviction for possessing a weapon under circumstances not manifestly appropriate for lawful uses was reinstated because the statute under which defendant was convicted was constitutional, and the trial court delivered an adequate charge.

Nash v. Board of Adjustment


A-56


Supreme Court of New Jersey


96 N.J. 97; 474 A.2d 241; 1984 N.J. LEXIS 2418


December 12, 1983, Argued  
April 19, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification to the Superior Court, Appellate Division.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant adjoining neighbors sought review of the opinion of the Superior Court (New Jersey), which found that appellee lot owner had established the criteria for a variance and that appellants had the right of first refusal to purchase the lot for a fair and reasonable offer price, which was defined as the value of the property as though the variance had been granted.


OVERVIEW: Appellee lot owner sought a variance from the township board of adjustment (board), which was granted. Appellant adjoining neighbors sought to set aside the variance. The superior court found that the variance was properly granted. The court affirmed, finding that appellee satisfied the two criteria for variance, that appellee would suffer exceptional or undue hardship if variance were not granted, and that the variance would not result in a substantial detriment to the public good or the zoning plan. The court noted that the board could grant a conditional variance and allow appellants to purchase the lot at a fair and reasonable price, to be determined by the fair market value of the property as though the variance had been granted. The court found that the fair market value was the amount appellants had been offered for the property assuming a house could be built on it, and not the lower amount that appellants had offered. The court denied appellants another opportunity to purchase the property at the higher amount because there was no reason to give appellants a second chance at that late date.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's opinion because appellee lot owner met the criteria for a variance and a fair and reasonable offer had to be what the property would be worth if the variance had been granted.

Romano v. Kimmelman


A-106


Supreme Court of New Jersey


96 N.J. 66; 474 A.2d 1; 1984 N.J. LEXIS 2416


November 29, 1983, Argued  
March 26, 1984, Decision Rendered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Opinion April 19, 1984.


PRIOR HISTORY: On certification to the Superior Court, Appellate Division and Monmouth County District Court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, individuals charged with drunk driving, alleged that certain breathalyzer models were unreliable and that their use as evidence of guilt was unconstitutional. On appeal from the dismissal of plaintiffs' complaint, the court, on certification to the Superior Court, Appellate Division (New Jersey), and the Monmouth County District Court (New Jersey), reviewed issues relating to the reliability of the breathalyzer models in question.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs were each charged with driving while under the influence of intoxicating liquor, based in part upon breathalyzer tests. Plaintiffs brought an action against defendants, state and others, alleging that certain breathalyzer models were unreliable and that their use to furnish evidence of guilt was unconstitutional. The impetus was a municipal court decision that those models were unreliable because of susceptibility to radio frequency interference. The appellate division affirmed the trial court's denial of class action certification and plaintiffs' motion for summary judgment on the ground of collateral estoppel but reversed the denial of defendants' motion to dismiss. The court certified the case, limited to issues relating to the reliability of the breathalyzer models in question. The court found that the breathalyzer models in question were scientifically reliable and accurate devices for determining the concentration of blood alcohol and that judicial notice could be taken of that reliability. The court found some radio frequency interference problems under certain circumstances and imposed some conditions for the admissibility of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate division that in effect dismissed the complaint. In reviewing issues related to the reliability of certain breathalyzer models, the court found that the breathalyzer models in question were scientifically reliable and accurate devices for determining the concentration of blood alcohol and that judicial notice could be taken of that reliability.

In re Coruzzi


D-2


Supreme Court of New Jersey


95 N.J. 557; 472 A.2d 546; 1984 N.J. LEXIS 2412


January 24, 1984, Argued  
March 20, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On an Order to Show Cause why respondent should not be removed or otherwise disciplined.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court instituted a complaint for the removal of respondent, a superior court judge, who was convicted of four counts of bribery. The court considered respondent's challenge to the validity of a statutory amendment to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:1B-5 that enabled the court to withhold respondent's pay indefinitely during removal proceedings.


OVERVIEW: Respondent, a superior court judge arrested after taking a bribe from a lawyer, was convicted of bribery. The court instituted a complaint for the removal of respondent. Respondent challenged a statutory amendment that enabled the court to withhold respondent's pay indefinitely during the removal proceedings pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:1B-5, the statute having previously limited that power to 90 days. The court held that the statutory amendment was valid in that it did not impose ex post facto punishment and that respondent had to be removed from office. The court stated that respondent sold his power, sold his judgments, and sold his independence. The court said that respondent not only betrayed his trust but also betrayed New Jersey's tradition of judicial honesty.


OUTCOME: The court removed respondent, a superior court judge, from office because the court found beyond a reasonable doubt that respondent engaged in misconduct in office. The court also held that the statutory amendment that enabled the court to withhold respondent's pay indefinitely during the removal proceedings was valid and not an ex post facto law.

Singer v. State


A-10


Supreme Court of New Jersey


95 N.J. 487; 472 A.2d 138; 1984 N.J. LEXIS 2409


September 27, 1983, Argued  
March 19, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification to the Superior Court, Appellate Division.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a state and its associated officials, challenged a decision of the Superior Court, Appellate Division (New Jersey), which awarded attorneys' fees to appellees, special state officials and employees, pursuant to the Civil Rights Attorney's Fees Awards Act, 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988, in appellees' action that invalidated the Casino Ethics Law, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 52:13D-17.1.


OVERVIEW: Appellees, special state officials and employees, obtained a declaratory judgment invalidating, on federal constitutional grounds, the Casino Ethics Law, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 52:13D-17.1, which prohibited state officers or employees from associating with casino licensees. On appeal from an award of attorneys' fees pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988, the court affirmed, holding that appellees were entitled to be considered "prevailing parties" for purposes of § 1988. Sufficient state official action was attendant upon the enactment of the Law to render appellees' claims of injury legally cognizable and relief pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 appropriate. Appellees' action sought a declaration of the operative Law's invalidity and an injunction against its threatened enforcement. Even without succeeding on their § 1983 claim, plaintiffs obtained substantially all of the relief they sought, thus demonstrating that the action they brought was a causal factor in the relief they ultimately achieved and that there was a legal basis for that relief. The court held that attorneys' fees should be awarded based upon reasonable hourly rates charged by attorneys of ordinary skill and experience.


OUTCOME: The judgment awarding appellees, special state officials and employees, attorneys' fees was affirmed, as appellees were prevailing parties in an action challenging the Casino Ethics Law. The matter was remanded for a determination of reasonable attorneys' fees.

In re Felmeister


D-3


Supreme Court of New Jersey


95 N.J. 431; 471 A.2d 775; 1984 N.J. LEXIS 2405


September 13, 1983, Argued  
February 29, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On leave to appeal from the District VII Ethics Committee.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an attorney disciplinary proceeding, respondent attorneys sought an interlocutory review and filed a motion to dismiss charges against them on the ground that a prohibition against broadcast advertising was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Respondent attorneys advised the ethics advisory committee that they planned to violate a prohibition against attorneys engaging in broadcast advertising. The committee advised respondents that it would not comment until the state advertising committee finished its review of the rule. Respondents broadcast their advertisements, and disciplinary action was initiated. Complainant Disciplinary Review Board alleged that respondents willfully and deliberately violated the ban on broadcast advertising in contempt of the state supreme court's rulemaking power. Respondents claimed that the broadcast restriction was unconstitutional and violated U.S. Const. amend. I. Respondents sought interlocutory review and moved to dismiss complainant's charges. The court remanded the cause for further proceedings by complainant. The court found that the constitutionality of the ban was not at issue and that the intentional violation of the rules of conduct was the paramount consideration. The proper course of conduct would have been for respondents to file a declaratory action to determine the constitutionality of the restriction.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion to dismiss. The court found that further ethical proceedings were required because respondents' willful violation of a disciplinary rule, not the constitutionality of the prohibition against attorney broadcast advertising, was at issue.

State v. Roth


A-85


Supreme Court of New Jersey


95 N.J. 334; 471 A.2d 370; 1984 N.J. LEXIS 2399


October 12, 1983, Argued  
February 7, 1984, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification to the Superior Court, Law Division, Union County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On certification sought by the state, the court reviewed a judgment of the Superior Court, Union County (New Jersey), which convicted defendant of first-degree aggravated sexual assault but sentenced defendant to five years' probation on condition that he undergo a specified in-patient rehabilitation program and continue visits to an organization for alcoholics.


OVERVIEW: At knifepoint, defendant forced a woman to perform a sexual act upon him. Defendant pleaded guilty to first-degree aggravated sexual assault. Tests revealed that defendant had a severe alcohol dependence and drug abuse problem. After receiving many letters urging that defendant not be imprisoned, the trial court sentenced defendant to five years' probation on condition that he undergo a specified in-patient rehabilitation program and continue visits to an organization for alcoholics. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. Noting that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:1-1 to 98-4 established an entirely new sentencing process, the court found that its appellate supervision of the sentencing process required it to remand for sentencing in accordance with the standards defined in its opinion. The court found, among other things, that the guidelines for sentencing were not followed because N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:44-1(d) established a presumption of imprisonment. The court also held that the state's right to appeal under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2C:44-1(f)(2) was constitutional under the double jeopardy clauses of N.J. Const. art. I, para. 11 and U.S. Const. amend. V.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court that convicted defendant of first-degree aggravated sexual assault but sentenced him to five years' probation with conditions because the court found that the guidelines for sentencing were not followed. The court remanded for further proceedings in accordance with its opinion.

Torchia v. Fisher


A-13


Supreme Court of New Jersey


95 N.J. 43; 468 A.2d 1061; 1983 N.J. LEXIS 2754


September 26, 1983, Argued  
December 22, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court, Appellate Division.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant airplane owner sought review of an order from the Superior Court, Appellate Division (New Jersey), which granted summary judgment in favor of plaintiffs in their action under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 6:2- 7. Plaintiffs brought their action against defendant airplane owner, defendant student's estate, and others, after they sustained property damages following a plane crash involving a plane stolen from defendant airplane owner.


OVERVIEW: Without permission, defendant student took an airplane that was stored in his school's facility. During the ensuing flight, defendant student crashed the plane into plaintiffs' homes. The crash destroyed one home and damaged the other. Defendant student was killed in the crash. Plaintiffs instituted an action pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 6:2-7 against defendant student's estate, defendant airplane owner, and others. Plaintiffs sought to recover for property damages and for personal injuries sustained by some of them. The lower court granted plaintiffs' motion for summary judgment. Defendant airplane owner contended that the plane was stolen and that the statute did not apply, and that it was unconstitutional. The state supreme court affirmed the lower court's decision, holding that defendant airplane owner, even as the owner of a stolen aircraft, was absolutely liable for ground damage caused by the airplane crash, and § 6:2-7 was constitutional because it served the legitimate purpose of shifting the loss caused by the airplane crash from plaintiffs, who were innocent victims on the ground, to defendant airplane owner.


OUTCOME: The lower court's grant of summary judgment in favor of plaintiffs in their action to hold defendant airplane owner liable for damages they sustained in a plane crash. The court held that defendant airplane owner was absolutely liable under the applicable statute even though the plane was used without defendant airplane owner's permission, and the controlling statute was constitutional.

Joseph H. Reinfeld, Inc. v. Schieffelin & Co.


A-106/107


Supreme Court of New Jersey


94 N.J. 400; 466 A.2d 563; 1983 N.J. LEXIS 2749; 1983-2 Trade Cas. (CCH) P65,669


April 19, 1983, Argued  
October 6, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification to the Superior Court, Appellate Division.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a distiller, its subsidiary importer, and authorized wholesaler, challenged the judgment of the Superior Court (New Jersey), which affirmed the order of the director of the Division of Alcoholic Beverage Control finding that appellants violated N.J. Stat. Ann. § 33:1-93.6. Appellants claimed denial of due process, equal protection and that the judgment violated the Sherman Act, 15 U.S.C.S. § 1.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, a distiller, its subsidiary importer, and authorized wholesaler, challenged the judgment of intermediate appellate court that affirmed the order of the director of the Division of Alcoholic Beverage Control finding that appellants violated N.J. Stat. Ann. § 33:1-93.6 by selling its products solely to the authorized wholesaler, rather than to all licensed wholesalers. Appellants claimed denial of due process, equal protection and that the judgment violated the Sherman Act, 15 U.S.C.S. § 1. The court affirmed, holding that the statute was to be liberally construed and that reincorporating in a new state or having the authorized wholesaler register as a "brand registrant" under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 13:2-33.1 was not a legitimate means of avoiding the anti-discrimination statute. The court also held that due process was not denied as there was a fair hearing before the division, that equal protection was not violated as the actions of the director were a rational regulation of an industry and not an arbitrary interference in a fundamental right. The actions of the director, as an action of the state, were not subject to the Sherman anti-trust act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the intermediate appellate court, holding that the director of the state liquor regulatory division correctly determined that appellants, a distiller, its subsidiary importer, and authorized wholesaler, violated the state anti-discrimination statute. The court held that the director's corrective actions were a constitutional and appropriate regulatory function of the state.

State v. Bruzzese


A-120


Supreme Court of New Jersey


94 N.J. 210; 463 A.2d 320; 1983 N.J. LEXIS 2738


March 8, 1983, Argued  
August 8, 1983, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court, Appellate Division.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of New Jersey sought review of a decision from the Superior Court, Appellate Division (New Jersey), which affirmed the trial court's decision to suppress evidence seized at defendant's home.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for burglary, theft, and criminal mischief. Counsel for defendant moved to suppress defendant's boots as evidence. The trial court granted defendant's motion, and the intermediate appellate court affirmed the decision. On appeal, the court held that the proper inquiry for determining the constitutionality of a search-and-seizure was whether the conduct the law enforcement official who undertook the search was objectively reasonable. Under the circumstances, the court held that the officer's execution of the arrest warrant in person was reasonable. Further, the circumstances of defendant's arrest disclosed that the officers exercised a legitimate investigatory technique in a proper and reasonable manner. The arrest of defendant at his home was reasonable, and the officer's act of following defendant upstairs was a reasonable consequence of defendant's own voluntary choice to go to his bedroom and get dressed. Finally, despite the absence of a search warrant, the seizure and inspection of defendant's boots was reasonable and constitutionally valid pursuant to the plain view doctrine.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the intermediate appellate court and remanded the cause for further proceedings.
