Kozlowski v. Kozlowski


A-172


Supreme Court of New Jersey


80 N.J. 378; 403 A.2d 902; 1979 N.J. LEXIS 1245


April 2, 1979, Argued  
June 25, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification to the Superior Court of New Jersey, Chancery Division, Morris County, whose opinion is reported at 164 N.J. Super. 162.
Kozlowski v. Kozlowski, 164 N.J. Super. 162, 395 A.2d 913, 1978 N.J. Super. LEXIS 1205 (Ch.Div., 1978)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant male challenged a decision of the Superior Court, Morris County (New Jersey) for appellant female. The primary issue on appeal was whether a man and a woman who were not married to each other, and who lived together without a promise of marriage, such as the parties in this case, had entered into a valid contract that was enforceable.


OVERVIEW: The parties in this case lived together for a total of 15 years excepting brief separations. Appellant provided financially while appellee provided services such as housekeeping, shopping, acting as mother to the children, escorting and accompanying appellant as he desired, and serving as hostess when necessary for his customers and business associates. The fact that that the parties had the same last name was coincident, because appellee's first husband had the same surname as appellant. Appellant challenged the lower court's decision for appellee. The case was transferred to the court prior to being heard by the appeals court. The court concluded that a man and a woman who were not married to each other and who lived together without a promise of marriage could enter into a contract that was enforceable regardless of whether the parties had a sexual relationship. The court concluded that any lawful agreement made by the parties was thus enforceable and was to be evaluated based upon the terms of the contract. The court affirmed the lower court judgment and remanded for further proceedings in the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court judgment and remanded the matter for such further proceedings as in the trial judge's sound discretion. The court was satisfied from a review of the record that the trial judge could reasonably have reached his factual and legal determinations on sufficient credible evidence present in the record as a whole, giving due regard to his ability to judge the credibility of the witnesses.

Klebanow v. Glaser


A-116


Supreme Court of New Jersey


80 N.J. 367; 403 A.2d 897; 1979 N.J. LEXIS 1248


March 5, 1979, Argued  
June 22, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court, Appellate Division, whose opinion is reported at 159 N.J. Super. 596 (1978).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court (New Jersey) affirming the determination of the state division of taxation that plaintiff's capital gains transaction resulted in a taxable event as contemplated by the Tax on Capital Gains and Other Unearned Income Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:8B-1 et seq. Plaintiff contended that the retroactive effect of the statute as applied to him was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, a former resident of New York, moved to New Jersey and sold securities, allegedly in reliance on the absence of a state capital gains tax. During the same year the state legislature enacted the Tax on Capital Gains and Other Unearned Income Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:8B-1 et seq., which applied to capital gains received on or after the first day of that year. The state division of taxation determined that plaintiff's capital gains transaction resulted in a taxable event as contemplated by the Act; the appellate division affirmed, and he sought review, contending that the retroactive effect of the statute as applied to him was unconstitutional because retroactivity was impermissible if the circumstances resulting in a taxable event were voluntarily created by a taxpayer. The court affirmed the judgment. It held that retroactive provisions of income tax statutes had invariably been held consistent with the due process clauses of U.S. Const. amends. V, XIV, and that the same rule would apply under N.J. Const. art. I, para. 1, especially in light of the need to apportion costs of government equitably and the reasonable notice provided of the pending enactment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, holding that the limited retroactive effect of the statute did not violate the state or federal constitutions under the circumstances, including the need to apportion the costs of government equitably and the reasonable notice provided by the public controversy and numerous income tax bills introduced in the legislature.

State v. Celmer

Supreme Court of New Jersey


80 N.J. 405; 404 A.2d 1; 1979 N.J. LEXIS 1240


March 6, 1979, Argued  
June 21, 1979, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Ocean Grove Camp Meeting Asso. of United Methodist Church v. Celmer, 444 U.S. 951, 100 S. Ct. 424, 62 L. Ed. 2d 321, 1979 U.S. LEXIS 3731 (1979)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification to the Superior Court, Appellate Division, whose opinion is reported at 157 N.J. Super. 242 (1978).
State v. Celmer, 157 N.J. Super. 242, 384 A.2d 894, 1978 N.J. Super. LEXIS 889 (N.J. Super. Ct., 1978)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a decision of the Superior Court, Appellate Division (New Jersey) that found defendant's drunk driving conviction, in intervenor municipal religious association's court, was invalid and violated U.S. Const. amend. I, and entered judgment of acquittal.


OVERVIEW: Intervenor was a religious group that established a camp meeting ground on 260 acres of land, which became the nucleus of a municipality. The Florida legislature granted intervenor the authority to carry out governmental functions. Defendant was convicted of drunk driving in intervenor's court. Defendant sought review, contending that intervenor's court was an improperly constituted tribunal in violation of the establishment of religion clause. The county court reversed the conviction and entered a judgment of acquittal. The lower appellate court reversed, reinstating the drunk driving conviction. The court reversed, acquitting defendant of the charges, holding that the statutory governmental authority granted to intervenor in N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40:97-1 et seq., was unconstitutional. A state was precluded from ceding governmental powers to a religious organization.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's drunk driving conviction and acquitted, holding that a state was precluded from ceding governmental powers to a religious organization. The statutory governmental authority granted to intervenor municipal religious association and its court was unconstitutional.

 

355 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


New Jersey Asso. on Correction v. Lan


A-141


Supreme Court of New Jersey


80 N.J. 199; 403 A.2d 437; 1979 N.J. LEXIS 1237


March 19, 1979, Argued  
June 8, 1979 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Decision Rendered April 2, 1979. Opinion Filed June 8, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Superior Court, Appellate Division, whose opinion is reported at 164 N.J. Super. 115 (1978).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state pursuant to N.J. Ct. R. 2:2-1(a)(1), appealed the judgment of the Superior Court, Appellate Division (New Jersey) reversing the trial court's judgment upholding the constitutionality of an institutional construction bond issue approved by the electorate. The court reviewed whether the three construction projects at issue comprised a single object in the intendment of the constitution.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found that a bond issue, approved by the electorate, providing for the construction of three separate public projects violated the state constitution. That court held that the projects were unrelated measures, disparate objects or works, improvidently combined provisions, leaving only as the proffered basis for relating the several purposes of the enactment the fact that buildings were to be constructed from the proceeds of the bonds. On review, the court reversed, holding that the grouping of related projects in one statute had become an established pattern, one apparently compatible with popular understanding and will, and legislative acceptance. The court perceived a sure "relatedness," fully meeting the constitutional norm among the institutional construction of the buildings, the purposes such institutions were to serve, the identity of those who were to be served thereby, and in the beneficent state resolve and commitment to them, i.e., the meeting of public responsibilities to the people of the state. The court found no constitutional imperative to strike down the determination of the legislature and the expressed will of the people.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court ,reversing the trial court's determination that the institutional construction bond issue approved by the electorate was constitutional, was itself reversed. There was a sufficient relatedness between the construction of institutional buildings, the purposes and public they were to serve, and the state's effort to meet its public responsibilities to pass constitutional muster.

 

356 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Garrow v. Elizabeth General Hospital & Dispensary


A-16


Supreme Court of New Jersey


79 N.J. 549; 401 A.2d 533; 1979 N.J. LEXIS 1215


November 13, 1978, Argued  
May 15, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification to the Superior Court, Appellate Division whose opinion is reported at 155 N.J. Super. 78 (1977).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant hospital challenged the ruling of the Superior Court of New Jersey which reversed the dismissal of plaintiff doctor's complaint seeking to restrain defendant from conducting a hearing on his application for membership to the hospital staff until plaintiff was permitted to examine all pertinent documents in defendant's possession.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff doctor filed a complaint accompanied by an order to show cause in the superior court, seeking to restrain defendant hospital from conduction a hearing on his application for membership to the hospital staff until he was permitted to examine all pertinent documents in defendant's possession. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the complaint. The trial court dismissed the complaint at the conclusion of the hearing. The superior court reversed and the court granted defendant's petition for certification. The court held that there was no crucial need which would justify judicial intervention because of the claim for discovery. The minutes particularized in some factual detail plaintiff's alleged inadequacies, and plaintiff would have become aware at the hearing of any other underlying data which defendant possessed. There was no reason to believe that defendant would not have afforded him additional time to prepare and present evidence in rebuttal. The court was in full agreement with the superior court that plaintiff was not entitled to a hearing by the entire board of trustees and that its delegation to a committee of this function was perfectly proper.


OUTCOME: The court modified a judgment entered by the superior court which reversed the ruling of the trial court. The court held that there was no crucial need which would justify judicial intervention because of a claim for discovery. However, the court was in full agreement with the superior court that plaintiff was not entitled to a hearing by the entire board of trustees, but that its delegation to a committee was proper.

In re Estate of Jackson


A-75


Supreme Court of New Jersey


79 N.J. 517; 401 A.2d 517; 1979 N.J. LEXIS 1213


February 20, 1979, Argued  
May 11, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from Superior Court, Appellate Division.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant minor child, through her mother, challenged a judgment from the Superior Court of New Jersey which affirmed the ruling of the trial court holding that appellee welfare board was entitled to reimbursement of welfare assistance furnished on behalf of minor from recovery in a personal injury action.


OVERVIEW: Appellant minor child suffered severe burns on her left leg after it became wedged between a wall and a steampipe in a housing authority apartment where she lived with her mother. Appellant's mother executed a written agreement pursuant N.J. Stat. Ann. § 44:10-4(a) to repay appellee welfare board from anticipated funds from a tort claim against the housing authority. After the tort action, appellee filed a complaint to recover the amount of assistance furnished. The trial court ruled in favor of appellee and the appellate division affirmed. An appeal on behalf of appellant was filed with the court as a matter of right. The court held that the agreement to repay and the right of appellee to collect payment was legal, but there were certain limitations on the exercise of the right. The court held that although the agreement to repay was signed by the mother on August 10, 1973, the trial court erroneously ordered repayment of the amount of welfare assistance furnished from May 1973, the alleged date of the accident. It was clear that the reimbursement provision of § 44:10 as it then existed, extended only to the amount of assistance granted from the date of the agreement to repay.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the superior court judgment, which affirmed the trial court judgment ordering repayment of welfare assistance furnished to appellant out of a tort recovery. The court held that an agreement to repay welfare assistance was legal, but that the statute that authorized repayment from personal injury suits extended only to the amount of assistance granted from the date of the agreement to repay, and not the date of the accident.

 

358 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Karcher v. Byrne


A-88


Supreme Court of New Jersey


79 N.J. 358; 399 A.2d 644; 1979 N.J. LEXIS 1200


February 5, 1979, Argued  
March 21, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court, Appellate Division, whose opinion is reported at 158 N.J. Super. 67 (1978).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review of the order of the Superior Court, Appellate Division (New Jersey), which affirmed the summary judgment granted by the trial court to respondent public officials denying appellants' challenge to the statutory formula for distributing state equalization aid to local school districts.


OVERVIEW: Appellant taxpayers challenged the formula for distributing state equalization aid to local school districts, under the Public School Education Act of 1975, N.J. Stat. Ann. 18A:7A-1, et seq., contending that it denied due process and equal protection and had a chilling effect on the free exercise of their religion by excluding sectarian school pupils from the distribution formula. Appellants also contended that the use of enrollment figures without use of attendance figures was contrary to the statutory requirement. The lower appellate court affirmed the trial court's summary judgment to respondent public officials. The court held that the statutory classification used in the state aid formula manifestly was neither arbitrary, invidious, nor discriminatory in a constitutional or any other sense. To include non-public school pupils in the formula would have raised serious questions as to its validity. Moreover, the legislative history of the enrolled and attending phrase and its administrative interpretation over the years supported the trial court's interpretation of the statute. It would frustrate the plan for state aid to be diminished solely because of pupil attendance figures.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the lower appellate court affirming the summary judgment of the trial court against appellant taxpayers and in favor of respondent public officials. Exclusion of non-public pupils from the formula for distributing state equalization aid to local school districts was not unconstitutional. Moreover, the use of enrollment figures and not attendance figures was supported by legislative history and interpretation.

 

359 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Senno


A-183/184/185


Supreme Court of New Jersey


79 N.J. 216; 398 A.2d 873; 1979 N.J. LEXIS 1192


May 23, 1978, Argued  
February 27, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification to Passaic County Court (A-183 State v. Senno). On certification to Union County Court (A-184 State v. Kenny). On appeal from Superior Court, Appellate Division (A-185 State v. Buonura). 
State v. Buonura, 76 N.J. 237, 386 A.2d 861, 1978 N.J. LEXIS 786 (1978)
State v. Kenny, 76 N.J. 236, 386 A.2d 861, 1978 N.J. LEXIS 784 (1978)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review in a consolidated appeal of the orders of Passaic County Court, Union County Court, and Superior Court, Appellate Division (New Jersey), which excluded appellants, charged with nonindictable offenses, from county pretrial intervention programs. Appellants contended their ineligibility violated their rights to equal protection.


OVERVIEW: Appellants were charged with nonindictable offenses and each sought admission to his county's pretrial intervention program. Eligibility in those counties was limited to persons charged with indictable offenses. Appellants claimed their exclusion violated equal protection. The court affirmed, holding that the equal protection rights of appellants had not been violated by their exclusion from pretrial intervention programs. Petty nonindictable offenses were not crimes, but were penal offenses, within the meaning of N.J. Ct. R. 3:28 and its accompanying guidelines. Thus, indictable offenses, which were crimes, were automatically eligible for admission to the program, but the program was intended to be permissive as to nonindictable offenses. This did not violate equal protection because the classification was not of a suspect class nor concerned with a fundamental right. Thus, it was sufficient that there was a rational basis for the classification, including the need for local flexibility in rehabilitating offenders and reducing court calendars, as well as local administrative and fiscal constraints. Territorial uniformity was not a constitutional requisite.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders of the lower courts denying appellants' entry into pretrial intervention programs. Appellants' equal protection rights had not been violated by their exclusion from the programs because there was a rational basis for making nonindictable offenses ineligible.

 

360 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Simon


A-4/5


Supreme Court of New Jersey


79 N.J. 191; 398 A.2d 861; 1979 N.J. LEXIS 1191


September 26, 1978, Argued  
February 26, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification to the Superior Court, Appellate Division.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order by the superior court (New Jersey) which affirmed defendant's conviction for conspiracy and other crimes based upon the misconduct of public officials while in office on the ground that any error involved in the use of special interrogatories at defendant's trial was harmless and thus did not require reversal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of conspiracy and other crimes based upon the misconduct of public officials while in office. The trial judge submitted to the jury special interrogatories relating to the applicability of the statute of limitations as a bar to the criminal prosecution. Defendant appealed his conviction. The court reversed and remanded, holding that the judge had committed plain error. The court held that the use of special interrogatories was improper because they had the prejudicial potential for leading the jury to adverse findings on the ultimate issue of guilt, and that risk was aggravated by the fact that the jury was directed to respond to the special interrogatories before it was asked to deliberate upon its general verdict, and without being fully instructed with respect to the law applicable to the criminal charges. The court held that the errors satisfied the requirements for plain error: the special interrogatories had the obvious capacity to lead the jury down the guilty trail, it could not be said beyond a reasonable doubt that they did not bring the jury to a result it might otherwise not have reached, and they were capable of producing an unjust result.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's convictions for conspiracy and other crimes based upon misconduct of public officials while in office. It was plain error to use special interrogatories at trial because they had the capacity to lead the jury down the guilty trail, it could not be said beyond a reasonable doubt that they did not bring the jury to a result it might otherwise not have reached, and they were capable of producing an unjust result.

In re Estate of Romnes


A-81


Supreme Court of New Jersey


79 N.J. 139; 398 A.2d 543; 1979 N.J. LEXIS 1185


December 12, 1977, Argued  
February 6, 1979, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargued September 25, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: On certification to the Superior Court, Appellate Division.
In re Estate of Romnes, 148 N.J. Super. 401, 372 A.2d 1115, 1977 N.J. Super. LEXIS 802 (App.Div., 1977)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners executors appealed an order of the superior court (New Jersey) which affirmed a decision by respondent New Jersey Transfer Inheritance Tax Bureau to deny a transfer inheritance tax return.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners executors filed a transfer inheritance tax return with respondent New Jersey Transfer Inheritance Tax Bureau. Petitioners listed among the decedent's assets a survivor's annuity that derived from an employee benefit plan of the decedent's employer. The annuity provided for annual fixed income payments to decedent's widow, which would continue during the remainder of her lifetime. In valuing the asset, petitioners claimed the right to take as a reduction the commuted value of all estimated federal income taxes that would be payable by the widow upon her annual receipt of those payments. Respondent denied the claim, as did the appellate court. The court affirmed the decisions. The court held that those taxes should not be taken into account to determine the market value of the annuity for New Jersey State Transfer Inheritance Tax purposes under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 54:34-1 et seq. The court held that it seemed reasonable to conclude that the legislature was anxious to increase revenues derived from the taxation of life estates and to adopt petitioners' position would go far to diminish or obliterate completely the gains foreseen and sought by this legislation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed respondent New Jersey Transfer Inheritance Tax Bureau's decision to deny petitioners executors' transfer inheritance tax return. The court held that petitioners could not take into account federal income taxes that would payable by a widow upon her receipt of a decedent's annuity payments in order to determine the market value of the annuity for transfer inheritance tax purposes.

Gillhaus Beverage Co. v. Lerner


A-20


Supreme Court of New Jersey


78 N.J. 499; 397 A.2d 307; 1979 N.J. LEXIS 1167


October 16, 1978, Argued  
January 11, 1979, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court, Appellate Division.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant licensed solicitors sought review of the order of the Superior Court, Appellate Division (New Jersey), which affirmed the summary judgment by the trial court in favor of the respondent director of the alcoholic beverage control division in appellants' class action to enjoin a questionnaire issued by respondent to all licensed solicitors in the wholesale liquor industry.


OVERVIEW: Respondent director of the alcoholic beverage division issued a questionnaire about a variety of trade practices to appellant licensed solicitors in the wholesale liquor industry, in the course of respondent's investigation into alleged illegal practices. The letter accompanying the questionnaire stated that if the recipient's truthful answers revealed unlawful activity, then the admission would be taken into consideration as a mitigating factor in the imposition of penalty, but failure to answer would result in sanctions. In appellants' class action to enjoin the questionnaire, the trial court granted summary judgment to respondent, which was affirmed by the lower appellate court. The court held that the use of the questionnaire as an investigative tool was well within the regulatory and investigative authority granted to respondent, under the Alcoholic Beverage Control Act, N. J. Stat. Ann. § 33:1-1 et seq. The grant by the legislature of such an extensive power was justified. However, the letter accompanying the questionnaire improperly sought to have licensees waive their fifth amendment rights, and the offending parts were struck down as illegal.


OUTCOME: The court modified the judgment of the lower appellate court which had affirmed the trial court's summary judgment in favor of respondent director of alcoholic beverage control division. Judgment was modified to require withdrawal of a letter which improperly intruded on appellant licensed solicitors' fifth amendment rights and resubmission of a questionnaire. As modified, judgment was affirmed.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state health department challenged the Superior Court Appellate Division (New Jersey) judgment reversing the per diem reimbursement rate set for respondent hospital pursuant to the Health Care Facilities Planning Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 26: 2H-1 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Appellant state health department determined that two of respondent hospital's proposed costs for the following year were not reimbursable, pursuant to the framework established for Medicaid and private insurance reimbursement rates under the Health Care Facilities Planning Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 26: 2H-1 et seq. The court remanded the matter to appellant for further proceedings.

The record supported appellant's decision regarding one of respondent's cost projections. The court remanded the second matter for further consideration by appellant.

Helmsley v. Ft. Lee


A-163/164/165/166/167 September Term 1977


Supreme Court of New Jersey


78 N.J. 200; 394 A.2d 65; 1978 N.J. LEXIS 238


May 22, 1978, Argued  
October 17, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification to Superior Court, Law Division, Bergen County (A-164/165 Americana Associates v. Borough of Fort Lee and A-166/167 New Jersey Realty Co. v. Borough of Fort Lee).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs in separate actions appealed the findings and determinations of the Superior Court, Law Division, Bergen County (New Jersey) regarding the constitutionality of a rent control ordinance.


OVERVIEW: Defendant municipality had enacted a rent control ordinance. Under the ordinance landlords could not increase rents greater than a certain percentage of the last prior rent amount during any calendar year. The ordinance effectively placed a ceiling rent increases. Landlords could seek hardship relief to supplement the automatic increases, but the hardship process was long and burdensome. Plaintiffs, owners of multiple-family dwellings challenged the ordinance, claiming that it was unconstitutional because plaintiffs were deprived of a fair return on their investment. The trial court initially permitted the landlords to increase their rents to the consumer price index. The municipality then revised the ordinance, allowing increases based on a different formula. A different set of plaintiffs challenged the new ordinance. The court consolidated cases and found that while the ordinance was invalid as to the limitation itself, the rate was severable from the ordinance, the rest of which was valid.


OUTCOME: Court modified the judgment of one case, and reversed the judgment of another, holding that the rent control ordinances were confiscatory and invalid after date certain, but the rate limitation was severable from the ordinance, the rest of which was valid.

Van Ness v. Borough of Deal


A-56


Supreme Court of New Jersey


78 N.J. 174; 393 A.2d 571; 1978 N.J. LEXIS 240


June 13, 1978, Argued  
October 16, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification to the Superior Court, Appellate Division, whose opinion is reported at 145 N.J. Super. 368 (1976).
Van Ness v. Deal, 145 N.J. Super. 368, 367 A.2d 1191, 1976 N.J. Super. LEXIS 623 (N.J. Super. Ct., 1976)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff public advocate sought partial review of a judgment by the Superior Court, (New Jersey), which reversed an earlier judgment in favor of respondent borough and allowed respondent to limit the number of people who were able to use a municipally owned beach.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff public advocate sought the opening of a beach and casino in respondent borough to the public, which had previously restricted use to casino members. Adjacent to the beach area was a beach, which was open to the public. Plaintiff's sole contention before the court was that the dry beach area immediately in front of the casino was subject to the public trust doctrine and should have been made available to the general public for proper enjoyment of public trust rights. The court reversed the judgment of the lower court in regard to the beach area because this area was under municipal ownership and dedication, was subject to the public trust doctrine, and all had the right to use and enjoy it. The public trust doctrine required that municipally owned upland sand area adjacent to the tidal waters must be open to all on equal terms and without preference. The court found that it was not significant that this area in its natural state was unsuitable for normal beach area and respondent's leveled a bluff and graded in order to create the beach area. The court held that respondent may adopt reasonable regulations as to the beach area under its exercise of police power.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's approval of a municipal restriction on the use of a dry beach area to casino members because this municipally owned land was subject to the public trust doctrine and the general public had the right to use and enjoy it.

Vornado, Inc. v. Hyland


A-149/150/151/152


Supreme Court of New Jersey


77 N.J. 347; 390 A.2d 606; 1978 N.J. LEXIS 213


April 11, 1978, Argued  
July 18, 1978, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal dismissed by Vornado, Inc. v. Degnan, 439 U.S. 1123, 99 S. Ct. 1037, 59 L. Ed. 2d 84, 1979 U.S. LEXIS 565 (1979)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification to the Superior Court, Law Division, Bergen County, whose opinion is reported at 148 N.J. Super. 343 (1977).
Vornado, Inc. v. Hyland, 148 N.J. Super. 343, 372 A.2d 667, 1977 N.J. Super. LEXIS 797 (N.J. Super. Ct., 1977)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, an attorney general, municipalities, and corporations challenged a judgment from the Superior Court of Bergen County (New Jersey), which held that plaintiff corporation adduced proof to establish the denial of equal protection under the Sunday Closing Law, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:171-5.8 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff corporation challenged the validity of the Sunday Closing Law, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:171-5.8 et seq. The trial court held that plaintiff showed that the statute denied plaintiff equal protection of the law. The trial court further held that the statute was invalid. On appeal, the court rejected plaintiff's contentions that the statute was vague and had selective and discriminatory enforcement. The court found that the rationale behind the statute had a rational basis in relation to the specific objective of the statute. This rationale included recognizing Sunday as a day of relaxation and for play, hobbies, and relaxation. The court concluded that the trial court did not undertake to establish that the classification set forth in the Sunday Closing Law was devoid of any rational relationship to its validated purposes on any conceivable basis. Therefore, the court held that plaintiff did not establish the invalidity of the Sunday Closing Law on equal protection or any other grounds. The judgment was reversed and the cause remanded.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment that plaintiff corporation was denied equal protection under state law was reversed because plaintiff failed to show the invalidity of the Sunday Closing Law on any conceivable grounds.

Resnick v. East Brunswick Township Board of Education


A-83/84


Supreme Court of New Jersey


77 N.J. 88; 389 A.2d 944; 1978 N.J. LEXIS 210


January 23, 1978, Argued  
July 11, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Superior Court, Appellate Division, whose opinion is reported at 144 N.J. Super. 474 (1976).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, board of education and religious organizations, appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court, Appellate Division (New Jersey) affirming a trial court's ruling that, to use school facilities, sectarian groups had to pay school boards a commercial rental rate, with a one-year limitation on sectarian groups' continued use of school premises.


OVERVIEW: Defendant school board allowed local groups to use school facilities during non-school hours, if they paid the cost of janitorial services. Third-party defendant religious organizations rented various facilities for religious services and instruction. Plaintiff alleged that use of schools by religious groups violated N. J. Stat. Ann. § 18A:20-34 and federal and state constitutions. The trial court held that the use of public schools for religious worship violated U.S. Const. amends. I and XIV. The trial court held that even use limited to education violated the prohibition in N.J. Const. art. I, para. 3, but that a rent schedule based on actual costs could cure that difficulty. The appellate division affirmed. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The court held that religious groups who fully reimbursed school boards for related out-of-pocket expenses could use school facilities on a temporary basis for religious services as well as educational classes. The court also held that the lower courts erred in requiring sectarian groups to pay a commercial rental rate and in placing a one-year limitation on their continued use of the school premises.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that required sectarian groups to pay school boards a commercial rental rate to use school facilities and placed a one-year limitation on continued use. The court held that religious groups could use school facilities on a temporary basis for religious services as well as educational classes if they paid full reimbursement for related out-of-pocket expenses.

Nicoletta v. North Jersey Dist. Water Supply Com.


A-25


Supreme Court of New Jersey


77 N.J. 145; 390 A.2d 90; 1978 N.J. LEXIS 209


November 14, 1977, Argued  
July 6, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification to the Superior Court, Appellate Division.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff police sergeant filed a petition for certification based on a decision by the Superior Court (New Jersey) that found plaintiff was not entitled to a hearing of the termination charges that had been filed against him by defendant public employer.


OVERVIEW: Defendant public employer discharged plaintiff police sergeant. Plaintiff filed an action challenging the validity of the termination and alleging that he had been discharged without notice of the charges against him, in violation of his constitutional right to due process. The trial court transferred the case to the appellate court. The appellate court remanded the case to defendant, who found sound reason existed for the termination of plaintiff because plaintiff had initiated a violent altercation with another officer. Plaintiff filed a petition for certification. The court first determined that plaintiff was entitled to hearing because plaintiff could be disqualified from future state service upon removal. Therefore, plaintiff had a protectable liberty interest pursuant to U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The court found that plaintiff was not notified of the charge against him or of other matters being investigated. Therefore, the court held that plaintiff was entitled to a post-termination hearing in order to protect plaintiff from future disqualification from public employment. However, plaintiff could not obtain reinstatement to his position. The decision was reversed.


OUTCOME: The decision that found plaintiff police sergeant was not entitled to a hearing on the termination charges was reversed because plaintiff was entitled to a hearing when plaintiff's eligibility for future employment with the state was at issue.

 

369 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Potter v. Charles V. Finch & Sons


A-93 September Term 1977


Supreme Court of New Jersey


76 N.J. 499; 388 A.2d 614; 1978 N.J. LEXIS 195


January 23, 1978, Argued  
June 7, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification to the Superior Court, Appellate Division.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant pedestrian sought review of an order of the Superior Court, Appellate Division (New Jersey), which granted summary judgment to respondent railroad and respondent employees under the provisions of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 48:12-152, which imputed negligence to appellant.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pedestrian brought an action against respondent railroad and respondent employees for injuries sustained while appellant was walking on railroad tracks. The trial court granted summary judgment to respondents pursuant to the provisions of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 48:12-152, which imputed negligence to any person injured while walking on railroad tracks and which barred recovery for such injuries from the company owning or operating the railroad. Appellant sought review. The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment to respondent railroad but reversed the judgment as to respondent employees. The court found that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 48:12-152 had to be strictly construed because it provided immunity from tort liability and could not be extended beyond its meaning. The court determined that the statute, by its terms, extended to the company owning or operating respondent railroad, but did not expressly include respondent employees in that protection. The court found that because the statute did not expressly extend to respondent employees, they could be held accountable for any negligent conduct. The case was remanded for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order granting judgment to respondent railroad in appellant pedestrian's negligence suit but reversed the judgment as to respondent employees because the statute imputing negligence to appellant for injuries incurred while walking on the train tracks of respondent railroad applied to respondent railroad only and not to respondent employees. The case was remanded for further proceedings relative to respondent employees.

State v. Miller


A-159


Supreme Court of New Jersey


76 N.J. 392; 388 A.2d 218; 1978 N.J. LEXIS 179


January 25, 1977, Argued  
May 24, 1978, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargued March 7, 1978.
Habeas corpus proceeding at Miller v. Fenton, 741 F.2d 1456, 1984 U.S. App. LEXIS 19413 (3d Cir. N.J., 1984)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Miller, 2011 N.J. Super. Unpub. LEXIS 788 (App.Div., Apr. 1, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: On certification to the Superior Court, Appellate Division.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed a decision from the Superior Court, Appellate Division (New Jersey), which reversed defendant's conviction for first degree murder on the ground that defendant's conviction was involuntary in the constitutional sense. Defendant also alleged that N.J. Ct. R. 1:8-2(d) was unconstitutional insofar as it permitted an alternative juror to be substituted for an original juror after deliberations had begun.


OVERVIEW: Waiving his Miranda rights, defendant confessed to murder during a tape-recorded interrogation at state police barracks. The confession was admitted into evidence over his objection that he had no recollection of the interrogation. During jury deliberations, an alternative juror was substituted for a juror who requested dismissal. On state's appeal of the reversal of defendant's conviction, the court held that the interrogation did not exceed proper bounds and the confession was not the result of intense and mind-bending psychological compulsion. The voluntariness of defendant's confession could properly have been determined by the trial court to be established beyond a reasonable doubt and, therefore, the confession was properly admitted into evidence. In this connection, the court rejected defendant's related contention that his confession was the product of strongly implied promises of an insanity defense and no prison sentence if he confessed. The court held that N.J. Ct. R. 1:8-2(d), in providing that for good cause shown an alternate juror could be substituted for a regular juror after deliberations had begun, did not offend the constitutional guaranty of trial by jury.


OUTCOME: The judgment reversing defendant's conviction for first degree murder was reversed on the ground that the use of a psychologically oriented technique of questioning defendant was not so inherently coercive as to result in an involuntary confession in the constitutional sense. Substitution of juror during deliberations was proper under the circumstances and did not offend the constitutional guaranty of trial by jury.

New Jersey Guild of Hearing Aid Dispensers v. Long


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New Jersey


75 N.J. 544; 384 A.2d 795; 1978 N.J. LEXIS 178


December 13, 1977, Argued  
March 9, 1978, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: New Jersey Guild of Hearing Aid Dispensers v. Long, 145 N.J. Super. 580, 368 A.2d 929, 1976 N.J. Super. LEXIS 643 (App.Div., 1976)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a non-profit guild and two of its officers, appealed an order of the Appellate Division (New Jersey ), which upheld the validity of regulations governing hearing aid dispensers, promulgated under the Hearing Aid Dispensers Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 45:9A-1 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, a non-profit guild and two of its officers, challenged an appellate court decision upholding the validity of state regulations enacted under a state statute governing the sale and distribution of hearing aids. The court rejected plaintiffs' arguments, which challenged the regulations as ultra vires on the grounds that they contravened legislative intent. Plaintiffs also contended that the regulations were preempted by a proposed federal regulatory scheme. The court dissolved the stay of enforcement and affirmed the judgment on the grounds that plaintiffs' contention that the statute never envisioned regulating the business aspects of hearing aid dispensing was without foundation, and the federal regulatory scheme implicitly allowed supplemental state regulation. The court, however, voided the state statute's pre-sale test requirements for hearing aids, because they were explicitly preempted by federal regulations.


OUTCOME: The stay of enforcement of the regulations was lifted and the judgment of the appellate court was affirmed as modified by the holding that the pre-sale hearing aid test requirements of the state regulations were preempted by the proposed federal regulatory scheme.

 

372 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Ballou v. State, Dep't of Civil Service


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New Jersey


75 N.J. 365; 382 A.2d 1118; 1978 N.J. LEXIS 153; 18 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 414; 17 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P8372


October 17, 1977, Argued  
February 6, 1978, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant claimant challenged the decision from the Superior Court, Appellate Division (New Jersey), which affirmed the rejection of appellant's claim that she was entitled to a civil service appointment that went to a veteran under N. J. Stat. Ann. § 11:27-4.


OVERVIEW: Appellant claimant challenged an appellate court decision which affirmed the rejection of appellant's claim to a civil service appointment that went to a veteran under N. J. Stat. Ann. § 11:27-4. Appellant scored the highest on the test for the position, but the job went to a veteran. Appellant claimed that the preference for veterans in civil service positions violated N. J. Const. art. VII, § 1, par. 2, and the Due Process and Equal Protection clauses of U. S. Const. amend. XIV. The court disagreed and affirmed the appellate court decision. The veterans' preference law was essentially similar to that which was "provided by law" at the time the Constitution was enacted, so the approval of the Constitution by the people of New Jersey was thus a virtual ratification of the scheme for veterans' preference in the civil service. Veterans had to demonstrate merit by passing a competitive test in order to be entitled to preference, so the preference was not violative of due process. Finally, the system was gender-neutral and did not violate equal protection merely because it disfavored women to a substantially greater degree than other non-veterans.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's decision rejecting appellant claimant's complaint regarding her entitlement to a civil service position. The statute granting a preference to veterans was approved by the voters when they adopted the state constitution, did not violate due process because it retained a merit component and was gender-neutral on its face so it did not violate the equal protection clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV.

 

373 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


K. S. B. Technical Sales Corp. v. North Jersey Dist. Water Supply Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New Jersey


75 N.J. 272; 381 A.2d 774; 1977 N.J. LEXIS 276


October 3, 1977, Argued  
December 23, 1977, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the North Jersey District Water Supply Commission and the State of New Jersey, and respondents, an individual and a corporation, sought review from a decision of the Appellate Division (New Jersey), which agreed with the trial court as to the invalidity of a "Buy American" provision in bidding specifications but held that the bids were void.


OVERVIEW: Respondent individual and corporation sought an adjudication that a "Buy American" provision in bidding specifications be declared invalid and its statutory foundation unconstitutional. The trial court declared the provision invalid but permitted the bids to stand. The court below agreed with the trial court as to the invalidity of the provision but held that the bids were void. On appeal, the court found that appellant water commission's purchases of materials and equipment for its water treatment plant were for governmental purposes and not with a view to use in the "production of goods for commercial sale." The purchases were exempted from the operation of Article III of the General Agreement on Tariffs and Trade, 62 Stat. 3681 (1948). Further, the court held that the "Buy American" statutes, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 52:33-2 and -3 did not violate the Commerce Clause. The "Buy American" statutes did not impermissibly interfere with the federal government's conduct of foreign affairs. The court reversed the judgment of the court below and directed that appellant water commission use the bids based on the specifications which included the "Buy American" provisions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's judgment, which agreed with the trial court as to the invalidity of a "Buy American" provision in bidding specifications but held that the bids were void. The "Buy American" statute governing appellant water commission's purchases of materials was excluded from the operation of GATT, and the New Jersey "Buy American" statutes did not constitute proscribed state action under the Commerce Clause.

 

374 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Saunders


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New Jersey


75 N.J. 200; 381 A.2d 333; 1977 N.J. LEXIS 274


April 26, 1977, Argued  
December 13, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Saunders, 142 N.J. Super. 287, 361 A.2d 111, 1976 N.J. Super. LEXIS 795 (N.J. Super. Ct., 1976)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision of the Appellate Division of the Superior Court (New Jersey) that affirmed the constitutionality of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:110-1, and his conviction, pursuant to the trial court's charge, for the lesser-included offense of fornication, after his acquittal on rape and assault charges. Defendant argued that the statute was unconstitutional because it outlawed conduct that the State had no power to prohibit.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for rape and assault after having what he claimed was consensual sex in a parking lot. The trial judge charged the jury that they could convict on the lesser-included offense of fornication under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:110-1 if defendant was not guilty of the other charges. The decision that upheld the constitutionality of the statute upon defendant's conviction for fornication was affirmed. On review, defendant argued that the statute was unconstitutional and selectively enforced. The court reversed and held that the statute prohibited defined conduct that involved a fundamental personal choice and therefore infringed upon defendant's constitutional right of privacy. The court also relied upon the constitutionally mandated zone of privacy that protected individuals from unwarranted governmental intrusion into matters of intimate personal concern. The court also concluded that the compelling state interests of preventing venereal disease or protecting marital relationships and the public morals did not justify the statute's impingement upon the fundamental right of privacy. Accordingly, judgments of acquittal were entered.


OUTCOME: The judgment that upheld the constitutionality of the fornication statute and affirmed defendant's conviction for the lesser-included offense of fornication was reversed. The statute prohibited defined conduct that involved a fundamental personal choice and was therefore unconstitutional because it infringed upon defendant's right of privacy. The statute's violation of the right to privacy was not justified by any compelling state interest.

State v. Zarinsky


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New Jersey


75 N.J. 101; 380 A.2d 685; 1977 N.J. LEXIS 264


September 19, 1977, Argued  
November 17, 1977, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Habeas corpus proceeding at Zarinsky v. Ricci, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 39547 (D.N.J., May 15, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Zarinsky, 143 N.J. Super. 35, 362 A.2d 611, 1976 N.J. Super. LEXIS 716 (App.Div., 1976)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision from the Appellate Division (New Jersey), which affirmed his conviction for murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted by a jury of first degree murder. He received the mandatory sentence of life imprisonment. On appeal, defendant contended his prosecution was barred by a statute of limitations. The court dismissed defendant's contentions, finding that there was no statute of limitations on a murder prosecution in New Jersey. The court noted the history of New Jersey legislative enactments with respect to criminal statutes of limitation was persuasive evidence that no limitation period for murder was intended. Accordingly, the court affirmed the lower court's decision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the lower court that affirmed defendant's murder conviction. The court held that the murder prosecution was not barred by any statute of limitations because there was no statute of limitations for murder in New Jersey.

 

376 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Tomarchio v. Greenwich


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New Jersey


75 N.J. 62; 379 A.2d 848; 1977 N.J. LEXIS 257


May 24, 1977, Argued  
November 3, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Tomarchio v. Greenwich, 71 N.J. 518, 366 A.2d 673, 1976 N.J. LEXIS 993 (1976)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent employer appealed the decision of the Workers' Compensation Division of Superior Court (New Jersey), which awarded benefits as a total dependent to petitioner surviving husband without the proof of a widower's dependency required by N.J. Stat. Ann. § 34:15-13(f), on grounds that the statute violated equal protection. Respondent argued that § 34:15-13(f) served a remedial purpose and facilitated administrative convenience.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner surviving husband brought a workers' compensation dependency claim against respondent, his deceased wife's employer. The workers' compensation judge found the dependency provision in N.J. Stat. Ann. § 34:15-13(f) unconstitutional on equal protection grounds because it afforded widows a conclusive presumption of total dependency but required dependency to be proved by widowers. On review, the administrative order as modified was affirmed. The court held that the gender based dependency provision in § 34:15-13(f) and the gender based distinctions that governed the duration and computation of workers' compensation benefits were unconstitutional. The statute was premised upon archaic and overbroad stereotypes regarding the economic dependency of women and denied female workers protection for their families equal to that afforded comparable male workers. The remedy that prospectively applied to widowers was upheld, but the award was modified to reflect decedent's full-time salary from respondent even though she was killed during concurrent part-time employment.


OUTCOME: The decision that awarded benefits as a total dependent to petitioner surviving husband without proof of his dependency on grounds that the statutory dependency provision violated equal protection was affirmed. The gender-based distinctions in the statutory provisions on dependency, duration, and computation were unconstitutional because they denied female workers protection for their families equal to that afforded comparable male workers.

 

377 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Corbitt


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New Jersey


74 N.J. 379; 378 A.2d 235; 1977 N.J. LEXIS 165


February 22, 1977, Argued  
October 6, 1977, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from a lower court (New Jersey), which convicted defendant of murder and arson and imposed a mandatory life sentence for the murder under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A: 113-3,4, as judicially altered. Defendant contended that the sentencing scheme violated his rights under the U.S. Const. amends. V, VI and the Equal Protection Clause.


OVERVIEW: Upon defendant's sentencing to life imprisonment for murder, the court granted certification limited to the issue of the validity of the mandatory life sentence upon a jury conviction for murder under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A: 113-3,4, as judicially altered. Defendant argued that a cited case invalidated the sentencing scheme because the difference in potential minimum sentences between that upon conviction after trial and that upon a plea of non vult infringed the U.S. Const. amend. V, impermissibly burdened the U.S. Const. amend. VI right to a jury trial, and denied equal protection to those defendants that went to trial. The court affirmed. The authority of the cited opinion was limited to a case of a choice between trial and plea of guilty when a possible consequence of the former, and only of the former, was the death penalty. Alternatively, any inducement to plead non vult and thereby to waive a right to trial was not an unnecessary device but a useful one and did not infringe on constitutional rights. Classification of offenders for purposes of fixing penalty were rationally related to proper legislative purposes and, therefore, defendant's equal protection claim failed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting defendant of murder and arson and sentencing him to life imprisonment. The court concluded that defendant's claims of constitutional violations lacked merit because the inducement to plead guilty was not improper, the cited opinion was inapplicable, and there was a rational basis for the classification of offenders for purposes of fixing penalty.

Franklin v. Board of Education


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New Jersey


74 N.J. 345; 378 A.2d 218; 1977 N.J. LEXIS 163


March 21, 1977, Argued  
September 22, 1977, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff township challenged a decision by the Appellate Division (New Jersey), which dismissed its appeal without making a decision on the merits of plaintiff's claim that the apportionment formula embodied in N.J. Stat. Ann § 18A:13-8 violated the "one-person, one-vote" rule of the United States Supreme Court.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff township contended that the apportionment formula of seats for a regional school board embodied in N.J. Stat. Ann § 18A:13-8 violated the "one-person, one-vote" rule of the United States Supreme Court. The lower court dismissed the action without making a decision on the merits. On appeal, the court found that the state had the burden of justifying the necessity for retaining the present apportionment formula embodied in N.J. Stat. Ann. § 18A:13-8. The court concluded that the facts of the case demonstrated a prima facie violation of the Equal Protection Clause of the United States Constitution. Accordingly, the court held that the scheme was invalid and N.J. Stat. Ann. § 18A:13-8 was unconstitutional as applied to the regional school district. The court also held that until a suitable plan was devised, the present members of the regional school board were to continue in office.


OUTCOME: The court held that the challenged apportionment scheme was invalid and N.J. Stat. Ann. § 18A:13-8 was unconstitutional as applied to a regional school district. The court held that until a constitutional plan was devised, the members of the regional school board were to continue in office.

Property Owners Asso. v. North Bergen


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New Jersey


74 N.J. 327; 378 A.2d 25; 1977 N.J. LEXIS 162; 5 A.L.R.4th 908


April 25, 1977, Argued  
September 12, 1977, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a township and a rent control board, sought review of an order from the Appellate Division (New Jersey), which declared amendments to a rent control ordinance to be invalid.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, a township and a rent control board, contended that an amendment to a rent control ordinance was a proper means of dealing with the problem of the lack of affordable housing for seniors. The lower court found the ordinance to be invalid. On appeal, the court affirmed the holding of the lower court, finding that compelled subsidization by landlords or by tenants who happen to live in an apartment building with senior citizens was an improper and unconstitutional method of solving the problem. The court noted that under its police power, a municipality could, in the interests of the general welfare, enact ordinances to assist senior citizens provided the relationship between the purposes and the classification was rational and sound and not an unconstitutional confiscation. The court however, held that the amendment in question amounted to an undue taking. Accordingly, the court affirmed the holding of the lower court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the lower court that declared amendments to a rent control ordinance invalid. The court held that compelled subsidization by landlords or tenants who happen to live in an apartment building with senior citizens was an improper and unconstitutional method of solving the housing shortage problem.

 

380 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Vinegra


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New Jersey


73 N.J. 484; 376 A.2d 150; 1977 N.J. LEXIS 220


September 13, 1976, Argued  
June 30, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Vinegra, 134 N.J. Super. 432, 341 A.2d 673, 1975 N.J. Super. LEXIS 772 (N.J. Super. Ct., 1975)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision from the Appellate Division (New Jersey), which reversed the trial court's decision and reinstated seven criminal counts against defendant that the trial court had dismissed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a public employee, was called before a grand jury to testify, and was questioned without being advised of his privilege against self-incrimination or his right to testimonial immunity under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:81-17.2a2. Defendant was subsequently charged with criminal conduct. The trial court found that defendant's rights pursuant to U.S. Const. Amend. V were violated, and dismissed seven of the eight counts in the indictment. The appellate court reversed, finding that pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:81-17.2a2, defendant's testimony before the grand jury could not be used against him in any subsequent criminal proceeding, and reinstated the dismissed counts. On review, the court found the remedy for violation of the Fifth Amendment privilege against self-incrimination was not dismissal of the indictment but rather suppression of the grand jury testimony. Therefore, the court held that dismissal of the first seven counts of the indictment was not required and that the immunity given defendant by N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:81-17.2a2 adequately protected his Fifth Amendment rights. The decision of the appellate court was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Decision of the appellate division that reversed the trial court's decision and reinstated seven criminal counts against defendant was affirmed. Defendant's remedy was to suppress grand jury testimony because defendant was not advised of his right against self-incrimination.

 

381 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


In re Tuso


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New Jersey


73 N.J. 575; 376 A.2d 895; 1977 N.J. LEXIS 225


March 7, 1977, Argued  
June 30, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: In re Petition of Tuso, 140 N.J. Super. 500, 357 A.2d 1, 1976 N.J. Super. LEXIS 941 (N.J. Super. Ct., 1976)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The commonwealth sought review of a decision of a Superior Court (New Jersey), which reversed a trial court order compelling appellee attorney to testify before a grand jury.


OVERVIEW: The commonwealth challenged an appellate court decision which reversed a trial court order compelling appellee attorney to testify before a grand jury. The appellate court based its decision upon the conclusion that the commonwealth did not need the information it was seeking from appellee. The commonwealth had admitted that it did not need the information for an indictment against the target, but wanted the testimony to assure a conviction. The commonwealth claimed that its evidence was hearsay and that it was within the discretionary powers of prosecution to elicit stronger evidence even if the hearsay would suffice to sustain an indictment, as distinguished from what would be required to make a prima facie case at trial. The court agreed and reversed the appellate division. The court found that the appellate court had found it unfair to order appellee to testify before the grand jury because appellee had been indicted for the same transaction. Appellee had full protection under the Witness Immunity Statute N. J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:81-17.3, so his constitutional right to remain silent was not violated by compelling him to testify against the target of the grand jury.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court decision which reversed an order compelling appellee attorney to testify at a grand jury proceeding. Although the information was not needed to secure an indictment, the commonwealth was properly exercising its discretionary power by seeking additional evidence to support its case against the target. Appellee, who was also indicted for the same transaction, had the protection of the Witness Immunity Act.

Montville v. Block 69, Lot 10


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New Jersey


74 N.J. 1; 376 A.2d 909; 1977 N.J. LEXIS 140


October 25, 1976, Argued  
June 9, 1977, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant corporate landowner sought review of a judgment of the N.J. Superior Court, Appellate Division that affirmed the trial court's decision that refused to find the In Rem Tax Foreclosure Act, N. J. Stat. Ann § 54:5-104.29 et seq, unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff municipality obtained a tax foreclosure judgment, barring all rights of redemption to defendant corporate landowner's property. Defendant sought to reopen that final judgment, on the grounds that the notice requirements of the In Rem Tax Foreclosure Act (Act), N. J. Stat. Ann § 54:5-104.29 et seq., fell short of U.S. Const. amend. XIV procedural due process. The Act required only notice by publication and posting. The trial court and the appellate division rejected appellant's argument, but on appeal, the court agreed with appellant. The court held that the notice provisions of the Act were unconstitutional under the state and federal constitutions, and it thus overruled City of Newark v. Yeskel, 5 N.J. 313 (1950), which upheld these procedures against similar constitutional objections. The court held that notice by publication was not constitutional in a foreclosure of tax delinquent premises where the municipality possessed the name and address of the owner but failed to give notice by mail or otherwise to that address. Accordingly, the court reversed the holding of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate division that refused to find the In Rem Tax Foreclosure Act unconstitutional. The court held that the notice requirements of the In Rem Tax Foreclosure Act violated due the Fourteenth Amendment.

Atlantic City v. Block C-11, Lot 11


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New Jersey


74 N.J. 34; 376 A.2d 926; 1977 N.J. LEXIS 141


October 25, 1976, Argued  
June 9, 1977, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant property owner challenged the order of the Appellate Division of the Superior Court (New Jersey) that affirmed the denial of defendant's motion to reopen the judgment entered against her in plaintiff city's lien claim under the In Rem Tax Foreclosure Act, N.J.S.A. 54:5-104.29 et seq. Defendant argued that she did not receive notice as required by the act, and that foreclosure of liens was not authorized against occupied land.


OVERVIEW: A judgment was entered in the tax lien foreclosure action brought by plaintiff city against defendant property owner. The denial of defendant's motion to reopen the judgment on procedural grounds and because the In Rem Tax Foreclosure Act, N.J.S.A. 54:5-104.29 et seq. did not apply was affirmed on appeal. On review, defendant claimed that she was denied procedural due process under the Act because the statute required individual notice to taxpayers of record. Defendant also argued that the statute did not permit foreclosure of liens against property that was occupied. The court disagreed and affirmed the appellate court's order. The court noted that defendant was not listed as a record owner of the subject property and that notice was sent to all owners of record in compliance with the statute. Consequently, notice was provided in accordance with the statute. The court also rejected defendant's claim that the statute only authorized foreclosure of liens on vacant land. The court noted that the legislature amended the statute to specifically allow foreclosure of liens on property that was either vacant or occupied.


OUTCOME: The order that affirmed the denial of defendant property owner's motion to reopen the judgment entered against her in plaintiff city's tax lien foreclosure claim was upheld. Defendant's name was not included in the list of record owners who did receive the requisite statutory notice of plaintiff's claim, and foreclosure was permitted on both vacant and occupied property in accordance with specific amendment to the applicable statute.

385 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Leonardis


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New Jersey


73 N.J. 360; 375 A.2d 607; 1977 N.J. LEXIS 209



May 31, 1977, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargued November 8, 1976.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Attorney General intervened to clarify the trial court's authority to order diversion of defendant into a pretrial intervention program when the prosecutor refused to consent to diversion. Previously, the court had reversed the Superior Court, Appellate Division (New Jersey) and held that by precluding from consideration all defendants charged with heinous offenses, the admission criteria failed to conform to the purposes of N.J. Ct. R. 3:28.


OVERVIEW: Appellants were charged with drug-related offenses and were denied admission to a pretrial intervention (PTI) program, an alternative to prosecution authorized under N.J. Ct. R. 3:28. In a prior ruling, the court reversed, holding that by precluding from consideration all defendants charged with heinous offenses, the county criteria for admission failed to conform to the rehabilitative purposes of N.J. Ct. R. 3:28. The court granted the Attorney General's motion to intervene for rehearing, especially to consider whether, in light of the doctrine of separation of powers, the court had the power to divert defendant over the prosecutor's objection. The court concluded that PTI fell within the practice and procedure over which the court had control through its rule-making powers. Rule 3:28 did not encroach upon the powers delegated to the legislative or executive branches of government. Judicial review over PTI was constitutionally authorized pursuant to the court's rule-making and adjudicatory powers. The scope of the court's review was properly limited to gross abuse of discretion by the prosecutor. Accordingly, the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed its judgment reversing the denial of the admission of appellants to a pretrial intervention program and affirmed the constitutionality of pretrial intervention (PTI). The court concluded that the court's control over and review of PTI decisions was grounded in the court's rule-making and adjudicatory powers and that such authority did not violate the doctrine of separation of powers.

Passaic County Probation Officers' Ass'n v. County of Passaic


A-82


Supreme Court of New Jersey


73 N.J. 247; 374 A.2d 449; 1977 N.J. LEXIS 201; 95 L.R.R.M. 2694


March 23, 1976, Argued  
May 16, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Passaic County Probation Officers' Asso. v. County of Passaic, 132 N.J. Super. 247, 333 A.2d 300, 1975 N.J. Super. LEXIS 883 (Ch.Div., 1975)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On the supreme court's own motion it certified plaintiff bargaining unit's cause from the Appellate Court of Passaic County (New Jersey) while plaintiff's appeal of judgment in favor of defendants, county and officials, was pending. Plaintiff's action was to enjoin the enforcement of a directive extending working hours and to compel defendant judges to negotiate in good faith with plaintiff.


OVERVIEW: Defendants, county and officials, implemented an extended work day for probation officers without first conferring with plaintiff, bargaining unit for the officers. Plaintiff sought relief via an action to enjoin the enforcement of the directive on the ground that it violated N.J. Stat. Ann. § 34:13A-5.3, and to compel defendant judges to negotiate in good faith with plaintiff as to proposed modifications of officers' hours of work. The trial court found that the directive did not modify any existing rule governing working conditions under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 34:13A-5.3, and was a reasonable exercise of defendant's administrative and supervisory authority over the officers pursuant to N.J. Stat. Ann. 2A:168-7. While this decision was on appeal by plaintiff, the supreme court on its own motion certified the cause. The court held that while the issue was not negotiable pursuant to the constitution, plaintiff was entitled to urge that this position be changed. The court ordered that plaintiff be accorded an opportunity to file a grievance with defendant judges and that defendant's should entertain such grievances in good faith. Judgment as modified was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Judgment denying plaintiff bargaining unit's attempt at enjoining enforcement of a directive from defendants, county and officials, to extend probation officers' work hours, and to compel defendant judges to negotiate in good faith with plaintiff's was affirmed as modified to allow for the filing of grievances and entertainment of such grievances by defendant judges in good faith.
