State v. Allen


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New Jersey


73 N.J. 132; 373 A.2d 377; 1977 N.J. LEXIS 189; 2 Media L. Rep. 1737


October 12, 1976, Argued  
April 22, 1977, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant newspapers challenged two New Jersey trial court orders preventing them from publishing any information about confessions made by two murder defendants and revealed during evidentiary hearings outside the presence of the juries, until the juries were sequestered to deliberate their verdicts. Appellants argued the orders were impermissible prior restraints.


OVERVIEW: The trial court in two murder cases entered orders preventing appellant newspapers from publishing any information about confessions made by the defendants and revealed during evidentiary hearings outside the presence of the juries, until the juries were sequestered to deliberate their verdicts. Appellants filed suit to challenge the orders, but the appellate court denied their appeal. Thereafter, appellants sought further review, arguing the orders were impermissible prior restraints. The reviewing court heard the matter because the issues were likely to recur and vacated the illegal orders. The court reasoned that newspapers have an absolute right or privilege to report events that transpire at a public court hearing. The court noted that the trial court could have used other means to insure that the juries did not have access to information about the confessions, such as sequestration, definitive instructions to not to read or listen to media reports of the trial and to decide the issues only on evidence presented in open court, or an in camera evidentiary hearing.


OUTCOME: The reviewing court vacated the orders preventing appellant newspapers from publishing any information about confessions made by two murder defendants until after the juries were sequestered to deliberate their verdicts. The court ruled that because the proceedings took place in open court, they were matters of public record and appellants had an absolute right to report thereon.

 

388 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


S.E.W. Friel Co. v. New Jersey Turnpike Authority


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New Jersey


73 N.J. 107; 373 A.2d 364; 1977 N.J. LEXIS 187


January 24, 1977, Argued  
April 20, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certification to the Superior Court, Appellate Division.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, injury victim and his employer, sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court, Appellate Division (New Jersey), which affirmed the trial court's decision that found that defendant New Jersey Turnpike Authority was a public entity, that plaintiff employer's claim was barred by the Tort Claim Act subrogation prohibition, and that plaintiff injury victim's claim was barred pursuant to N. J. Stat. Ann § 59:8-9.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff injury victim was in an accident on the New Jersey Turnpike, while he was driving a truck for plaintiff employer, and was hospitalized for several weeks. The trial court denied plaintiffs' motion for leave to file a late notice of claim under the New Jersey Tort Claims Act (Act), N. J. Stat. Ann § 59:1-1 et seq. (1976-77). The appellate division affirmed, holding that defendant New Jersey Turnpike Authority was a public entity within the meaning of the Tort Claims Act; therefore the provision of the Act barring subrogation actions, N. J. Stat. Ann § 59:9-2(e), served to preclude the claims of plaintiff employer and the injury claim of plaintiff injury victim was foreclosed because he had not timely sought permission to file a late claim. Plaintiffs appealed, contending that defendant was not a "public entity," and that plaintiff injury victim had presented sufficient reasons to allow late filing of his claim. The court reversed in part and remanded, holding that defendant was a public entity, but that plaintiff injury victim should have been allowed to file a late claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the superior court that held that defendant New Jersey Turnpike Authority was a public entity within the meaning of the Tort Claims Act and that plaintiff employer's claims were barred by reason of the prohibition against subrogation claims. The court reversed that portion of the judgment that barred the claim of plaintiff injury victim and remanded the cause to the trial court.

 

389 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Fobe Associates v. Board of Adjustment


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New Jersey


74 N.J. 519; 379 A.2d 31; 1977 N.J. LEXIS 170


May 25, 1976, Argued  
March 23, 1977, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant developer sought review of a judgment from a lower court (New Jersey), which approved the action of respondent, a board of adjustment, in denying a N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40:55-39 (d) zoning variance to appellant to build an apartment house in a restricted single-family residence district and which held that the zoning ordinance prohibiting multi-family-residential buildings was valid.


OVERVIEW: Appellant developer sought review of a judgment in favor of respondent, a board of adjustment, approving a denial of a N.J. Stat. Ann. § 40:55-39 (d) variance to build an apartment house in a restricted single-family residence district and rejecting the claim that a zoning ordinance was invalid because it absolutely prohibited multi-family-residential buildings. The court affirmed. The zoning ordinance at issue was valid as a legislative judgment that the best interests of the municipality were served by preserving its character as a single-family residential community. The application for the variance was properly denied because there was no finding that without appellant's project, the general welfare inherent in the provision of more multi-family housing would not be attained. The court declined to resolve the knotty issue of whether such housing inherently benefitted the general welfare because respondent's findings in support of the variance denial were not arbitrary and were based on substantial evidence. The acceptance into evidence of the planning board's resolution disapproving the variance was commonplace procedure, and reasonable notice of it was given to appellant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of respondent, a board of adjustment, that denied a zoning variance to appellant developer to build an apartment house in a restricted single-family zone and that held that the restrictive ordinance was valid. The ordinance preserving the character of the single-family residential community was a valid legislative judgment, and respondent's denial of the variance was supported by substantial evidence.

 

390 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Pascack Asso. v. Washington


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New Jersey


74 N.J. 470; 379 A.2d 6; 1977 N.J. LEXIS 169


May 25, 1976, Argued  
March 23, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Pascack Asso. v. Washington, 131 N.J. Super. 195, 329 A.2d 89, 1974 N.J. Super. LEXIS 459 (N.J. Super. Ct. Law Div., 1974)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff developer sought review of a judgment from a lower court (New Jersey), which reversed a trial court's judgment holding that defendant township's zoning ordinance, limiting residential development to single-family lots, was invalid and which remanded the denial of plaintiff's application for a variance to build multi-family housing.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff developer brought an action against defendant township challenging the denial of a variance to build multi-family housing and the validity of a zoning ordinance limiting residential development to single-family lots. The lower court reversed a judgment that the ordinance was invalid and that remanded the variance denial. On appeal, the court affirmed the validity of the zoning ordinance with a modification approving the trial court's judgment that an ordinance amendment increasing lot sizes was invalid. Plaintiff misplaced reliance on a cited case. The cited case involved a developing municipality, and defendant was a fully developed one. The cited case did not displace established principles disfavoring judicial intervention in local zoning decisions. The decision to keep the municipality free from multi-family development was not an arbitrary one. The general shortage of multi-family housing did not effectively amend the ordinance to require such housing. The requirement that all municipalities must zone for housing for all categories of the population, middle and upper classes as well as low and moderate income, was not applicable to a fully developed municipality.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment setting aside the trial court adjudication of illegality of an ordinance for failure to zone for multi-family residential use and the remand of defendant township's denial of a variance to plaintiff developer to build multi-family housing. The court concluded that the zoning ordinance legitimately preserved the single-family character of defendant, a fully developed municipality.

Inganamort v. Ft. Lee


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New Jersey


72 N.J. 412; 371 A.2d 34; 1977 N.J. LEXIS 247


October 26, 1976, Argued  
March 2, 1977, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant borough and officials appealed a New Jersey trial court judgment granting plaintiff landlords' motion for summary judgment in an action challenging Fort Lee Ordinance No. 72-1, a local rent control ordinance. Defendants argued that the court erred in finding that the governing body could not extend the ordinance by a resolution and that as a result the ordinance expired after the original one-year term.


OVERVIEW: Defendant borough enacted Fort Lee, N.J., Ordinance No. 72-1, a local rent control ordinance. Section 20 of the ordinance provided that it remained in effect for up to one year, but could be extended by the governing body by resolution extending said term from year to year. After defendant borough and officials extended the term for two consecutive years, plaintiff landlords filed suit against defendants, arguing that the ordinance could not be extended by resolution. The trial court granted plaintiffs' motion for summary judgment. On review, defendants argued that the trial court erred in finding that the governing body could not extend the ordinance by a resolution and that as a result the ordinance expired after the original one-year term. The court reversed the trial court judgment. The court ruled that § 20 was invalid because reenactment of rent control legislation that initially was required to be enacted by ordinance could not be accomplished by resolution. However, the court ruled that § 20 was properly severable from the remainder of the ordinance because without that section, rents would be regulated in the borough as long as the housing emergency continued.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court judgment granting plaintiff landlords' motion for summary judgment in an action challenging a local rent control ordinance. The court ruled that although the ordinance was improperly extended by resolution after the expiration of its original term, it was still valid because the invalid portion was severable.

 

392 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Cirelli v. Ohio Casualty Ins. Co.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New Jersey


72 N.J. 380; 371 A.2d 17; 1977 N.J. LEXIS 245


November 8, 1976, Argued  
February 28, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Cirelli v. Ohio Casualty Ins. Co., 133 N.J. Super. 492, 337 A.2d 405, 1975 N.J. Super. LEXIS 844 (N.J. Super. Ct., 1975)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant insurer appealed the trial court's declaratory judgment for plaintiff regarding the invalidity of plaintiff's insurance liability policy reimbursement provisions and the trial court's award of counsel fees to plaintiff.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, a New Jersey resident, was injured in an accident that occurred in New York. The other driver was a New York resident. As required by the New Jersey Automobile Reparation Reform Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 39:6A-1 et seq., plaintiff's liability insurance policy included a personal injury protection clause (PIP). The PIP clause subrogated defendant insurer to plaintiff's rights against a third party and required plaintiff to reimburse defendant insurer from any recovery. The trial court held that the reimbursement clause was invalid, entered judgment for plaintiff, and awarded plaintiff counsel fees. On review, the court affirmed the fee award holding that N.J. Ct. R. 4:42-9(a)(6) allowed a counsel fee award in plaintiff's liability insurance policy action. However, the court held that the reimbursement and subrogation provisions of plaintiff's policy were valid. The court held that reimbursement and subrogation clauses were a safeguard against double recovery of PIP payments in situations where an accident occurred out-of-state between a New Jersey vehicle and a vehicle from another jurisdiction. Judgment was affirmed as modified.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed counsel fees for plaintiff because counsel fees were permitted by court rule; however, court held that reimbursement and subrogation clauses of plaintiff's liability insurance policy were valid since the clauses protected against double recovery of personal injury protection payments where accident occurred outside the state between a vehicle of New Jersey and a vehicle from another state. Judgment was affirmed as modified.

Vreeland v. Byrne


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New Jersey


72 N.J. 292; 370 A.2d 825; 1977 N.J. LEXIS 238


November 23, 1976, Argued  
February 11, 1977, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a judicial candidate, a governor, a senator, and a state, filed notices of appeal to the Superior Court (New Jersey) and then moved for direct certification and for an accelerated argument of its ruling that the nomination of the judicial candidate was unconstitutional as being in violation of N.J. Const. art. IV, § 5, para. 1.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, taxpayer groups and eight senators, filed declaratory judgment actions challenging the judicial candidate's nomination to the state supreme court. The trial court ruled that the nomination of the judicial candidate was unconstitutional because it violated N.J. Const. art. IV, § 5, para. 1. Defendants filed notices of appeal to the trial court and then moved for direct certification and for an accelerated argument. The court granted defendants' motions for direct certification and for an accelerated argument and affirmed the judgment that the nomination was invalid because N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:1A-8 was to be deemed deleted from N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:1A-6 et seq. The court held that the nomination of the judicial candidate contravened N.J. Const. art. IV, § 5, para. 1. The court concluded that the presence of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:1A-8 rendered the salary statute unconstitutional in its application to legislator-appointees, and hence was to be excised, and it followed that the nomination could not have stood. The court also concluded that N.J. Stat. Ann. § 2A:1A-8 constituted special legislation.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motion of defendants for direct certification and for an accelerated argument and affirmed the judgment that the nomination of the judicial candidate was invalid in plaintiffs' declaratory judgment actions. The court found that an unconstitutional statutory provision was to be deleted from the salary adjustment statute.

Schaad v. Ocean Grove Camp Meeting Asso. of United Methodist Church


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New Jersey


72 N.J. 237; 370 A.2d 449; 1977 N.J. LEXIS 237; 2 Media L. Rep. 1354


October 6, 1975, Argued  
February 10, 1977, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargued April 6, 1976.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant town meeting association sought review of a decision by the trial court (New Jersey) that granted summary judgment to appellee news service owner in an action brought by appellee that challenged the validity of ordinances and the enabling statute that prohibited driving and other activities on Sundays.


OVERVIEW: Appellee news service owner was charged with violating ordinances by appellant town meeting association that prohibited Sunday driving. Appellee sought to deliver newspapers that were not received from the publisher until nearly midnight the previous evening. Subsequent to the charges, appellee brought an action challenging the ordinances and sought injunctive relief against their enforcement. A motion for summary judgment filed by appellee was granted by the trial court which held that the prohibition of newspaper deliveries on Sundays was an unconstitutional infringement of the freedom of the press and that the Sunday driving ban was a violation of the guaranty of due process under U.S. Const. amend. XIV. Upon review, the court essentially held that any attempt to restrict the freedom of the press had to be justified by a clear public interest. It was an undue restriction of the press to prohibit Sunday delivery when the result would be no paper delivery at all on Sundays. The judgment of the trial court was modified with an order stating that the ordinances, though not invalid, could not be enforced with respect to appellee's Sunday paper delivery service.


OUTCOME: The court modified the judgment of the trial court that found the ordinances were an unconstitutional infringement on the freedom of the press and remanded the entry to declare that appellant town meeting association could not enforce the ordinances with respect to appellee news service owner's delivery of the newspaper on Sunday mornings because doing so would interfere with a free press.

Oakwood at Madison, Inc. v. Madison


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New Jersey


72 N.J. 481; 371 A.2d 1192; 1977 N.J. LEXIS 252


March 5, 1973, Argued  
January 26, 1977, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargued January 8, 1974. April 14, 1975. November 18, 1975.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant township sought review of a decision by the trial court (New Jersey) that invalidated a current zoning ordinance that was amended after plaintiffs, two corporations and class of individuals seeking housing, challenged the validity of the ordinance previously adopted by the township.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, corporations and individuals seeking housing, challenged the validity of the local zoning ordinance that had been adopted by defendant township in 1970. Defendant was required to amend the ordinance, which it did in 1973. Thereafter, the trial court invalidated the 1973 amendment. Prior to adopting the 1970 ordinance, the township declared a moratorium on residential construction other than owner-occupied single family dwellings while the adoption of a new master plan and zoning ordinance was pending. A claim challenging the moratorium resulted in a deadline for submitting the master plan and adopting the new zoning ordinance. The result was the 1970 ordinance which failed to provide for low-cost housing needs. In determining that the 1973 ordinance was also invalid, the trial court found that the ordinance did not provide the opportunity to meet a fair share of the regional burden for low and moderate income housing needs. The court modified the trial court's decision that invalidated the ordinance and directed the municipality to revise the ordinance to meet the obligations to zone for least cost housing.


OUTCOME: The court modified the decision of the trial court that invalidated the zoning ordinance and instead remanded for defendant township to revise the ordinance to create the opportunity for a fair and reasonable share of the least cost housing needs of the region.

In re Heller


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New Jersey


73 N.J. 292; 374 A.2d 1191; 1977 N.J. LEXIS 205


October 13, 1976, Argued  
January 20, 1977, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: In re Heller, 150 N.J. Super. 25, 374 A.2d 1211, 1975 N.J. Super. LEXIS 922 (N.J. Super. Ct., 1975)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, pharmacist and pharmacy, sought review of the judgment from the Superior Court, Appellate Division (New Jersey), that affirmed the decision of respondent New Jersey State Board of Pharmacy which revoked appellants' professional licenses for grossly unprofessional conduct pursuant to the Pharmacy Act (Act), N.J. Stat. Ann. 45:14-12 and imposed a civil penalty for appellants' violations of the Act.


OVERVIEW: In license revocation proceedings, respondent New Jersey Board of Pharmacy charged that appellants, pharmacy and pharmacist, improperly sold a controlled dangerous substance which constituted grossly unprofessional conduct in violation of the Pharmacy Act, N.J. Stat. Ann. 45:14-12. The complaint did not mention the assessment of civil penalties. Respondent found appellants guilty, entered a revocation order, and assessed a civil penalty in an amount equal to the minimum amount of unjust profit appellants received. The appellate court affirmed. Appellants sought review and argued that their conduct was not expressly prohibited by statute and the monetary penalty was improperly imposed. The supreme court affirmed the trial and appellate court's judgment regarding appellants' license revocation because respondent was permitted to take action without its powers being limited to the express provisions of the statute. However, the assessment of the monetary penalty was reversed because respondent failed to follow the statutory procedure in imposing the penalty, and failed to afford notice to appellants that it intended to consider such a penalty.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the license revocation of appellant, pharmacy and pharmacist because respondent New Jersey Board of Pharmacy was permitted to take action under the Pharmacy Act without its powers being limited to the express provisions of the statute. However, the supreme court reversed the assessment of the monetary penalty because respondent failed to afford notice to appellants that it intended to consider such a penalty.

Borland v. Bayonne Hospital


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New Jersey


72 N.J. 152; 369 A.2d 1; 1977 N.J. LEXIS 230


November 22, 1976, Argued  
January 13, 1977, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed summary judgments of the chancery division, affirmed by the Appellate Division (New Jersey), alleging they were denied procedural due process by not being allowed a plenary hearing, and were denied substantive due process by the statutory scheme of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 17:48-1 et seq., which established defendant hospital service plan's reimbursement rates to defendant hospitals.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff patients brought suit against defendant service plan, hospitals, and New Jersey Commissioners of Health and Insurance, contending that rates agreed to by the service plan and the hospitals, and approved by Commissioners, for reimbursement to hospitals for health care services rendered to service plan subscribers, were lower than the actual cost of such services, so the hospitals had to charge non-service plan patients higher rates, which subsidized the service plan's program. Plaintiffs claimed they were denied procedural due process in not being allowed a plenary hearing to investigate processes by which service plan reimbursement rates to the hospitals were established and were denied substantive due process by statutory scheme of N.J. Stat. Ann. § 17:48-1 et seq. The lower courts granted summary judgment to defendants, and plaintiffs appealed. The court affirmed and held that regulation of reimbursement rates paid by the service plan was reasonable and consistent with public health care policy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment in favor of defendant hospitals, service plan, New Jersey Commissioner of Health, and New Jersey Commissioner of Insurance, finding that regulation of reimbursement rates paid by defendant service plan's hospital service corporation was reasonable and supported by the state's public policy in the field of public health care.

Lige v. Montclair


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New Jersey


72 N.J. 5; 367 A.2d 833; 1976 N.J. LEXIS 220; 13 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 1697; 12 Empl. Prac. Dec. (CCH) P11,258


May 10, 1976, Argued  
November 30, 1976, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, Director of the New Jersey Division of Civil Rights (director) and potential firefighter, challenged an order of the Superior Court, Appellate Division (New Jersey), that held that appellant director exceeded his statutory power and violated the discrimination principles of N.J. Const. art. I, para. 5 and the Law Against Discrimination, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 10:5-1 et seq., when he adopted a discriminatory quota regime.


OVERVIEW: Appellant potential firefighter ("firefighter") was denied a firefighting position because he failed a written test and commenced suit against respondents, town, mayor, and commissioners. Appellant firefighter alleged that the testing and selecting procedures were fair in form but discriminatory in operation against blacks. Appellant Director of the New Jersey Division of Civil Rights (director) found for appellant firefighter and ordered respondents to reevaluate all black applicants in accordance with non-discriminatory standards and to promote one qualified black applicant for every one qualified white applicant. The appellate court reversed. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that appellant director's order was violative of N.J. Const. art. I, para. 5 and was beyond the power entrusted to appellant director under N.J. Stat. Ann. § 10:5-17. The court reasoned that to rectify the wrongs of the past by a method of racial quotas defeated the very purpose of the Law Against Discrimination, N.J. Stat. Ann. § 10:5-1 et seq.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court because appellant Director of the New Jersey Division of Civil Rights exceeded his statutory power and violated both New Jersey law and the New Jersey Constitution when it set up a discriminatory quota regime to alleviate alleged past discrimination.

 

399 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


State v. Fariello


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New Jersey


71 N.J. 552; 366 A.2d 1313; 1976 N.J. LEXIS 175


December 2, 1975, Argued  
November 10, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Fariello, 133 N.J. Super. 114, 335 A.2d 582, 1975 N.J. Super. LEXIS 803 (N.J. Super. Ct., 1975)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Appellate Division (New Jersey), which affirmed his convictions for possession of marijuana with intent to manufacture and distribute, maintaining premises resorted to by persons for the purpose of unlawful manufacture and distribution of marijuana, and possession of a dangerous knife.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of possession of marijuana with intent to manufacture and distribute, maintaining premises resorted to by persons for the purpose of unlawful manufacture and distribution of marijuana, and possession of a dangerous knife. The court below affirmed those convictions, and defendant appealed. The court held that a judge's failure to record or summarize a police officer's oral comments given at the time he sought a search warrant for defendant's home made the subsequent testimony by the officer at the suppression hearing unreliable and inadmissible. The court also held that the officer's affidavit in support of the warrant was insufficient to show probable cause. The court found, however, that the discovery of a weapon on defendant resulted from a search incident to a lawful arrest, and was not unlawfully connected to the illegal search of defendant's home. The court reversed the convictions for possession with intent to manufacture and distribute marijuana, and of maintaining premises resorted to by persons for the purpose of unlawful manufacture and distribution of marijuana, and the judgment of conviction for possession of a dangerous knife was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's judgment affirming defendant's convictions for drug offenses because the trial court had erred in admitting evidence and testimony by a police officer regarding the evidence. The court affirmed the conviction for possession of a dangerous knife because the knife was found while searching defendant incident to a lawful arrest.

 

400 of 2470 DOCUMENTS


Panzino v. Continental Can Co.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New Jersey


71 N.J. 298; 364 A.2d 1043; 1976 N.J. LEXIS 151


March 23, 1976, Argued  
September 29, 1976, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Panzino v. Continental Can Co., 135 N.J. Super. 206, 343 A.2d 100, 1975 N.J. Super. LEXIS 692 (N.J. Super. Ct., 1975)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner claimant sought review of a judgment of the Appellate Division (New Jersey), which reversed an award in favor of petitioner by the compensation court in petitioner's claim for occupational hearing loss, filed six years after retiring from his employment with respondent corporation.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner claimant filed a claim for occupational hearing loss six years after retiring from his employment with respondent corporation. As the Workmen's Compensation Act (the act) was then written, this time span exceeded the permissible period within which such a claim was required to be filed. Two months before his claim was heard, however, a statutory amendment abrogated the time limitation. The compensation court ruled that petitioner was entitled to prevail because the claim came within the statutory amendment. The appellate court reversed, holding that the amendment should only be given prospective application. The petitioner appealed. The court reversed the appellate court and reinstated the judgement of the compensation court, holding that that statutory amendment to the act had to be interpreted retroactively to allow claims to be filed within two years of discovery of the nature of a disability. The court rejected respondent's argument that giving the act a retrospective interpretation trampled its vested right to impose the bar of the earlier time limitation, noting that the defense related to the compensation court's lack of jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court and reinstated the judgment of the compensation court. The court held that the amendment to the Workmen's Compensation Act would be applied retroactively to cover the claim of petitioner claimant, who filed his claim for occupational hearing loss six years after retiring from his employment with respondent corporation, but within one month of discovering that the impairment was work-related.
